<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">  (Redirected from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/w/index.php?title=Novofedorivka_incident&amp;redirect=no" title="Novofedorivka incident">Novofedorivka incident</a>)</span></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="hatnote" role="note">For the 1783 event, see <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Empire" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Empire">Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Empire</a>.</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Timeline of the annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">Timeline of the annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation</a>.</div>

<td colspan="2">
<table style="width:100%;margin:0;padding:0;border:0">
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Date</th>
<td>20 February 2014 – 19 March 2014<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-1">[1]</a></sup> (24 days)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Location</th>
<td><span class="location"><a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a></span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Result</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Little_green_men_(Ukrainian_crisis)" title="Little green men (Ukrainian crisis)">Russian masked troops</a> invade and occupy key Crimean locations, including airports and military bases, following <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Putin</a>'s orders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FT15Mar15_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FT15Mar15-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-airport_seizure_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-airport_seizure-3">[3]</a></sup></li>
<li>The head of <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Navy" title="Ukrainian Navy">Ukrainian Navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denis_Berezovsky" title="Denis Berezovsky">Admiral Berezovsky</a>, defects, followed later by half of the Ukrainian military stationed in the region<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></li>
<li>Russian forces seize the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_of_Crimea" title="Supreme Council of Crimea">Supreme Council (Crimean parliament)</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Crimea" title="Council of Ministers of Crimea">Council of Ministers of Crimea</a> is dissolved and a new pro-Russian <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Crimea" title="Prime Minister of Crimea">Prime Minister</a> installed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beast_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beast-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN1_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN1-8">[8]</a></sup></li>
<li>The new Supreme Council declares the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a> to be an independent, self-governing entity, then holds a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimean_referendum,_2014" title="Crimean referendum, 2014">referendum on the status of Crimea</a> on 16 March, which results in a majority vote to join the Russian Federation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-march6bbc_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-march6bbc-9">[9]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="#Accession_treaty_and_immediate_aftermath">Treaty signed</a> between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea_(country)" title="Republic of Crimea (country)">Republic of Crimea</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Kremlin" title="Moscow Kremlin">Kremlin</a> on 18 March to formally initiate Crimea's accession to the Russian Federation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Armed_Forces" title="Ukrainian Armed Forces">Ukrainian Armed Forces</a> are evicted from their bases on 19 March by Crimean protesters and Russian troops. Ukraine subsequently announces the withdrawal of its forces from Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></li>
<li>Russia suspended from <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Eight" title="Group of Eight">G8</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_sanctions_during_the_Ukrainian_crisis" title="International sanctions during the Ukrainian crisis">International sanctions</a> introduced on Russia</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>

<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-top:1px dotted #aaa;">3 protesters died (2 pro-Russian and 1 pro-Ukrainian)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RallyDeaths_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-RallyDeaths-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-censor_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-censor-30">[30]</a></sup><br/>
All deaths were not related directly to military activities</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukrainian</a> territory of <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a> was <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">annexed</a> by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a> on 18 March 2014. Since then, the <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a> has been administered as two <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia" title="Federal subjects of Russia">Russian federal subjects</a>—the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a> and the city of <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a>, which, until 2016, were grouped in the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Federal_District" title="Crimean Federal District">Crimean Federal District</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The annexation was preceded by <a href="/wiki/Russian_military_intervention_in_Ukraine_(2014%E2%80%93present)" title="Russian military intervention in Ukraine (2014–present)">a military intervention</a> by Russia in Crimea, which took place in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Ukrainian_revolution" title="2014 Ukrainian revolution">2014 Ukrainian revolution</a> and was part of wider <a href="/wiki/2014_pro-Russian_unrest_in_Ukraine" title="2014 pro-Russian unrest in Ukraine">unrest across southern and eastern Ukraine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Putin17April_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Putin17April-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 22–23 February, Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> convened an all-night meeting with security services chiefs to discuss extrication of the deposed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_President" title="Ukrainian President">Ukrainian President</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a>, and at the end of that meeting Putin had remarked that "we must start working on returning Crimea to Russia."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yahoo_News_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo_News-34">[34]</a></sup> On 23 February 2014, pro-Russian demonstrations were held in the Crimean city of Sevastopol. On 27 February <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Little_green_men_(GRU)" title="Little green men (GRU)">masked Russian troops without insignia</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FT15Mar15_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-FT15Mar15-2">[2]</a></sup> took over the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_of_Crimea" title="Supreme Council of Crimea">Supreme Council</a> (parliament) of Crimea,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time1_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-time1-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters1_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters1-36">[36]</a></sup> and captured strategic sites across Crimea, which led to the installation of the pro-Russian <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Aksyonov" title="Sergey Aksyonov">Aksyonov</a> government in Crimea and the declaration of <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_of_the_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Declaration of Independence of the Republic of Crimea">Crimea's independence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Washington_Post_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Washington_Post-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zakon_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-zakon-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ukraine considers the annexation to be a violation of international law and agreements by Russia, including <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Agreement on Establishing the Commonwealth of Independent States in 1991</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helsinki_Accords" title="Helsinki Accords">Helsinki Accords</a>, <a href="/wiki/Budapest_Memorandum_on_Security_Assurances" title="Budapest Memorandum on Security Assurances">Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons of 1994</a> and <a href="/wiki/Partition_Treaty_on_the_Status_and_Conditions_of_the_Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Partition Treaty on the Status and Conditions of the Black Sea Fleet">Treaty on friendship, cooperation and partnership between the Russian Federation and Ukraine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The event <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_reactions_to_the_2014_Crimean_crisis" title="International reactions to the 2014 Crimean crisis">was condemned by many world leaders</a> as an illegal annexation of Ukrainian territory, in violation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1994_Budapest_Memorandum" title="1994 Budapest Memorandum">1994 Budapest Memorandum</a> on sovereignty and territorial integrity of Ukraine, signed by Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> It led to the other members of the then <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G8" title="G8">G8</a> suspending Russia from the group,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> then introducing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_sanctions_during_the_2014_pro-Russian_unrest_in_Ukraine" title="International sanctions during the 2014 pro-Russian unrest in Ukraine">the first round of sanctions</a> against the country. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> also rejected the vote and annexation, adopting a <a href="/wiki/Non-binding_resolution" title="Non-binding resolution">non-binding</a> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_68/262" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 68/262">resolution</a> affirming the "territorial integrity of Ukraine within its internationally recognised borders".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CCTV_UNR_C.3DU_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-CCTV_UNR_C.3DU-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_A_RES_68_262_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN_A_RES_68_262-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following a <a href="/wiki/Crimean_status_referendum,_2014" title="Crimean status referendum, 2014">Crimean referendum</a>, held on 16 March 2014, in which separation was favoured by a large majority of voters, the UN resolution also "underscores that the referendum having no validity, cannot form the basis for any alteration of the status of [Crimea]."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_A_RES_68_262_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN_A_RES_68_262-43">[43]</a></sup> The resolution calls upon all States and international organizations not to recognize or to imply the recognition of Russia's annexation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_A_RES_68_262_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-UN_A_RES_68_262-43">[43]</a></sup> In 2016, UN General Assembly reaffirmed non-recognition of the annexation and condemned "the temporary occupation of part of the territory of Ukraine — the Autonomous Republic of Crimea and the city of Sevastopol".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Russian Federation opposes the "annexation" label,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> with Putin defending the referendum as complying with the principle of <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">self-determination</a> of peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> In July 2015, Russian prime minister <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a> said that Crimea had been fully integrated into Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Historical_background_of_the_2014_pro-Russian_unrest_in_Ukraine#Crimea" title="Historical background of the 2014 pro-Russian unrest in Ukraine">Historical background of the 2014 pro-Russian unrest in Ukraine § Crimea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_transfer_of_Crimea.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="841" data-file-width="886" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/The_transfer_of_Crimea.jpg/300px-The_transfer_of_Crimea.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/The_transfer_of_Crimea.jpg/450px-The_transfer_of_Crimea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/The_transfer_of_Crimea.jpg/600px-The_transfer_of_Crimea.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_transfer_of_Crimea.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Decree of the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet "About the transfer of the Crimean Oblast". Supreme Council Herald, 9 March 1954.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Crimea became part of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> in 1783, when the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Crimean Khanate</a> was <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Empire" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Empire">annexed</a>, then became part of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic</a> until 1954.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Initially it was incorporated into the Empire as <a href="/wiki/Taurida_Oblast" title="Taurida Oblast">Taurida Oblast</a> but in 1795 it was merged into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Novorossiysk_Governorate" title="Novorossiysk Governorate">Novorossiysk Governorate</a> and then, in 1802, transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Taurida_Governorate" title="Taurida Governorate">Taurida Governorate</a>. A series of short-lived governments (<a href="/wiki/Crimean_People%27s_Republic" title="Crimean People's Republic">Crimean People's Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Regional_Government" title="Crimean Regional Government">Crimean Regional Government</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Socialist_Soviet_Republic" title="Crimean Socialist Soviet Republic">Crimean SSR</a>) were established during first stages of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a>, but they were followed by <a href="/wiki/White_movement" title="White movement">White Russian</a> (<a href="/wiki/General_Command_of_the_Armed_Forces_of_South_Russia" title="General Command of the Armed Forces of South Russia">General Command of the Armed Forces of South Russia</a>, later <a href="/wiki/South_Russian_Government" title="South Russian Government">South Russian Government</a>). In October 1921, the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Crimean Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Crimean Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian SFSR</a> was instituted. After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Deportation_of_the_Crimean_Tatars" title="Deportation of the Crimean Tatars">deportation of all of the indigenous Crimean Tatars</a>, the Crimean ASSR was stripped of its autonomy in 1946 and was downgraded to the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Oblast" title="Crimean Oblast">status</a> of an <a href="/wiki/Oblasts_of_Russia" title="Oblasts of Russia">oblast</a> of the Russian SFSR.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%90%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%9C%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%A5%D1%80%D1%83%D1%89%D0%BE%D0%B2_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="254" data-file-width="354" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/%D0%90%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%9C%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%A5%D1%80%D1%83%D1%89%D0%BE%D0%B2_2009.jpg/180px-%D0%90%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%9C%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%A5%D1%80%D1%83%D1%89%D0%BE%D0%B2_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/%D0%90%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%9C%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%A5%D1%80%D1%83%D1%89%D0%BE%D0%B2_2009.jpg/270px-%D0%90%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%9C%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%A5%D1%80%D1%83%D1%89%D0%BE%D0%B2_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/35/%D0%90%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%9C%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%A5%D1%80%D1%83%D1%89%D0%BE%D0%B2_2009.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%90%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%9C%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%A5%D1%80%D1%83%D1%89%D0%BE%D0%B2_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ukrainian stamp to honor Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> who transferred Crimea from <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russia</a> to <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic">Ukraine</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1954, the Crimean Oblast was <a href="/wiki/1954_transfer_of_Crimea" title="1954 transfer of Crimea">transferred</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_SFSR" title="Russian SFSR">Russian SFSR</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_SSR" title="Ukrainian SSR">Ukrainian SSR</a> by decree of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidium_of_the_Supreme_Soviet_of_the_USSR" title="Presidium of the Supreme Soviet of the USSR">Presidium of the Supreme Soviet</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>.</p>
<p>In 1989, under <a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">perestroika</a>, the Supreme Soviet declared that the deportation of the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatars" title="Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars</a> under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Josef_Stalin" title="Josef Stalin">Stalin</a> had been illegal,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> and the mostly <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslim</a> ethnic group was allowed to return to Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1990, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_(council)" title="Soviet (council)">Soviet</a> of the Crimean Oblast proposed the restoration of the Crimean ASSR.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The oblast conducted a <a href="/wiki/Crimean_sovereignty_referendum,_1991" title="Crimean sovereignty referendum, 1991">referendum</a> in 1991, which asked whether Crimea should be elevated into a signatory of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Union_Treaty" title="New Union Treaty">New Union Treaty</a> (that is, became a <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">union republic</a> on its own). By that time, though, the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> was well underway. The Crimean ASSR was restored for less than a year as part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Ukraine" title="Soviet Ukraine">Soviet Ukraine</a> before <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_independence_referendum,_1991" title="Ukrainian independence referendum, 1991">Ukrainian independence</a>. Newly independent <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> maintained Crimea's <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Autonomous Republic of Crimea">autonomous status</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_of_Crimea" title="Supreme Council of Crimea">Supreme Council of Crimea</a> affirmed the peninsula's "sovereignty" as a part of Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The autonomous status of Crimea was limited by Ukrainian authorities in 1995.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Ukraine)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Ukraine)">Ukrainian Foreign Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Volodymyr_Ohryzko" title="Volodymyr Ohryzko">Volodymyr Ohryzko</a> accused Russia of giving out <a href="/wiki/Russian_passport" title="Russian passport">Russian passports</a> to the population in Crimea and described it as a "real problem" given Russia's declared policy of military intervention abroad to protect Russian citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 August 2009, anti-Ukrainian demonstrations were held in Crimea by ethnic Russian residents. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sergei_Tsekov&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sergei Tsekov (page does not exist)">Sergei Tsekov</a> (of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Bloc_(party)" title="Russian Bloc (party)">Russian Bloc</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> and then deputy speaker of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimean_parliament" title="Crimean parliament">Crimean parliament</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>) said then that he hoped that Russia would treat Crimea the same way as it had treated <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia">South Ossetia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Crimea is populated by an <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Ukraine" title="Russians in Ukraine">ethnic Russian</a> majority and a minority of both ethnic <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> and Crimean Tatars, and thus <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Ukraine" title="Demographics of Ukraine">demographically</a> possessed one of the Ukraine's largest Russian populations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Euromaidan_and_the_Ukrainian_revolution">Euromaidan and the Ukrainian revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Euromaidan and the Ukrainian revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Euromaidan" title="Euromaidan">Euromaidan</a> and <a href="/wiki/2014_Ukrainian_revolution" title="2014 Ukrainian revolution">2014 Ukrainian revolution</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Euromaidan_Night_of_11_December_18.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1326" data-file-width="2048" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Euromaidan_Night_of_11_December_18.jpg/220px-Euromaidan_Night_of_11_December_18.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Euromaidan_Night_of_11_December_18.jpg/330px-Euromaidan_Night_of_11_December_18.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Euromaidan_Night_of_11_December_18.jpg/440px-Euromaidan_Night_of_11_December_18.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Euromaidan_Night_of_11_December_18.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Euromaidan in Kiev, 11 December 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Euromaidan" title="Euromaidan">Euromaidan</a> protest movement began in Kiev in late November 2013 after President <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_Regions" title="Party of Regions">Party of Regions</a>, suspended the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93European_Union_Association_Agreement" title="Ukraine–European Union Association Agreement">Ukraine–European Union Association Agreement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atlantic800k_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-atlantic800k-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economist.com_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-economist.com-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kyivpost.com_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-kyivpost.com-66">[66]</a></sup> Yanukovych won the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_presidential_election,_2010" title="Ukrainian presidential election, 2010">2010 presidential election</a> with strong support from voters in the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Autonomous Republic of Crimea">Autonomous Republic of Crimea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ukraine" title="Southern Ukraine">southern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Ukraine" title="Eastern Ukraine">eastern Ukraine</a>. The Crimean autonomous government strongly supported Yanukovych and condemned the protests, saying they were "threatening political stability in the country". The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_of_Crimea" title="Supreme Council of Crimea">Crimean autonomous parliament</a> said that it supported the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azarov_Government" title="Azarov Government">government</a>'s decision to suspend negotiations on the pending association agreement and urged Crimeans to "strengthen friendly ties with Russian regions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 February 2014, the Presidium of the Supreme Council considered holding a referendum on the peninsula's status, and asked the Russian government to guarantee the vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chronicles_of_Alienation_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicles_of_Alienation-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Security_Service_of_Ukraine" title="Security Service of Ukraine">Security Service of Ukraine</a> (SBU) responded by opening a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Criminal_case" title="Criminal case">criminal case</a> to investigate the possible "subversion" of Ukraine's territorial integrity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> On 20 February 2014, during a visit to <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Supreme_Council_of_Crimea" title="Chairman of the Supreme Council of Crimea">Chairman of the Supreme Council of Crimea</a> <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Konstantinov_(politician)" title="Vladimir Konstantinov (politician)">Vladimir Konstantinov</a> stated that the <a href="/wiki/1954_transfer_of_Crimea" title="1954 transfer of Crimea">1954 transfer of Crimea</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic">Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> had been a mistake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chronicles_of_Alienation_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicles_of_Alienation-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Euromaidan protests <a href="/wiki/2014_Ukrainian_revolution" title="2014 Ukrainian revolution">came to a head</a> in late February 2014, and Yanukovych and many of his ministers fled the capital on 22 February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ukraine_crisis_timeline_BBC_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ukraine_crisis_timeline_BBC-73">[73]</a></sup> After his flight, opposition parties and defectors from the Party of Regions put together a parliamentary quorum in the <a href="/wiki/Verkhovna_Rada" title="Verkhovna Rada">Verkhovna Rada</a> (the Ukrainian parliament), and voted on 22 February to remove Yanukovych from his post on the grounds that he was unable to fulfil his duties,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EnUkrRev_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-EnUkrRev-74">[74]</a></sup> although this legislative removal lacked the required three-quarter vote of sitting Rada members according to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ukraine" title="Constitution of Ukraine">constitution in effect at the time</a>, which the Rada also voted to suspend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interfax1_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-interfax1-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RadioFreeEurope_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-RadioFreeEurope-77">[77]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arseniy_Yatsenyuk" title="Arseniy Yatsenyuk">Arseniy Yatsenyuk</a> was appointed by the Rada to serve as the head of a <a href="/wiki/Caretaker_government" title="Caretaker government">caretaker government</a> until new presidential and parliament elections could be held. This <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Yatsenyuk_Government" title="First Yatsenyuk Government">new government</a> was recognised internationally, though the Russian government said that these events had been a "<a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a>", and that the caretaker government was illegitimate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Anti-Maidan" title="Anti-Maidan">Anti-Maidan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_military_intervention_in_Ukraine_(2014%E2%80%93present)" title="Russian military intervention in Ukraine (2014–present)">Russian military intervention in Ukraine (2014–present)</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crimean_crisis_begins">Crimean crisis begins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Crimean crisis begins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9E%D1%82%D1%80%D1%8F%D0%B4_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%8B_%D0%9A%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D1%81_%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%88%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D0%B2_%D1%86%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B0_%D1%84%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D1%83%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%9A%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D1%85%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8F%D1%8E%D1%82_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BC%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="800" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/%D0%9E%D1%82%D1%80%D1%8F%D0%B4_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%8B_%D0%9A%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D1%81_%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%88%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D0%B2_%D1%86%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B0_%D1%84%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D1%83%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%9A%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D1%85%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8F%D1%8E%D1%82_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BC%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0.jpg/250px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/%D0%9E%D1%82%D1%80%D1%8F%D0%B4_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%8B_%D0%9A%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D1%81_%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%88%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D0%B2_%D1%86%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B0_%D1%84%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D1%83%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%9A%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D1%85%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8F%D1%8E%D1%82_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BC%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0.jpg/375px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/%D0%9E%D1%82%D1%80%D1%8F%D0%B4_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%8B_%D0%9A%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D1%81_%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%88%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D0%B2_%D1%86%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B0_%D1%84%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D1%83%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%9A%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D1%85%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8F%D1%8E%D1%82_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BC%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0.jpg/500px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9E%D1%82%D1%80%D1%8F%D0%B4_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%8B_%D0%9A%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D1%81_%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%88%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D0%B2_%D1%86%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B0_%D1%84%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D1%83%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%9A%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D1%85%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8F%D1%8E%D1%82_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BC%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"Crimean self-defence" members, 2 March 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The February 2014 <a href="/wiki/2014_Ukrainian_revolution" title="2014 Ukrainian revolution">revolution</a> that ousted Ukrainian president <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a> sparked a political crisis in Crimea, which initially manifested as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2014_Crimean_crisis#23_February" title="Timeline of the 2014 Crimean crisis">demonstrations</a> against the new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Yatsenyuk_Government" title="First Yatsenyuk Government">interim Ukrainian government</a>, but rapidly escalated. In January 2014 the <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> city council had already called for formation of "people's militia" units to "ensure firm defence" of the city from "extremism".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimean_parliament" title="Crimean parliament">Crimean parliament</a> members called for an extraordinary meeting on 21 February. <a href="/wiki/Mejlis_of_the_Crimean_Tatar_People" title="Mejlis of the Crimean Tatar People">Crimean Tatar Mejlis</a> chairman <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Dzhemilev" title="Mustafa Dzhemilev">Mustafa Dzhemilev</a> said that he suspected that the meeting was arranged to call for Russian military intervention in Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> In response to this, the <a href="/wiki/Security_Service_of_Ukraine" title="Security Service of Ukraine">Security Service of Ukraine</a> (SBU) said that it would "use severe measures to prevent any action taken against diminishing the territorial integrity and sovereignty of Ukraine".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[nb 1]</a></sup> The party with the largest number of seats in the Crimean parliament (80 of 100), the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_Regions" title="Party of Regions">Party of Regions</a> of Ukrainian president <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a>, did not discuss Crimean secession, and were supportive of an agreement between President Yanukovych and <a href="/wiki/Euromaidan" title="Euromaidan">Euromaidan</a> activists to end the unrest that was struck on the same day in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 22–23 February, Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> convened an all-night meeting with security services chiefs to discuss extrication of the deposed Ukrainian president, Viktor Yanukovych, and at the end of that meeting Putin had remarked that "we must start working on returning Crimea to Russia."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yahoo_News_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo_News-34">[34]</a></sup> On 23 February <a href="/wiki/2014_pro-Russian_unrest_in_Ukraine" title="2014 pro-Russian unrest in Ukraine">pro-Russian demonstrations</a> were held in the Crimean city of Sevastopol.</p>
<p>Crimean prime minister <a href="/wiki/Anatolii_Mohyliov" title="Anatolii Mohyliov">Anatolii Mohyliov</a> said that his government recognised the new provisional government in Kiev, and that the Crimean autonomous government would carry out all laws passed by the Ukrainian parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Simferopol" title="Simferopol">Simferopol</a>, a pro-Euromaidan rally of between 5,000–15,000 was held in support of the new government, and demanding the resignation of the Crimean parliament; attendees waved Ukrainian, Tatar, and European Union flags.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> Meanwhile, in Sevastopol, thousands protested against the new Ukrainian government, voted to establish a parallel administration, and created civil defence squads with the support of the Russian <a href="/wiki/Night_Wolves" title="Night Wolves">Night Wolves</a> motorcycle club. Protesters waved Russian flags, chanted "Putin is our president!", and said they would refuse to further pay taxes to the Ukrainian state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-russiarally_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-russiarally-90">[89]</a></sup> Russian military convoys were also alleged to be seen in the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-russiarally_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-russiarally-90">[89]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Kerch" title="Kerch">Kerch</a>, pro-Russian protesters attempted to remove the Ukrainian flag from atop city hall and replace it with the flag of Russia. Over 200 attended, waving Russian, orange-and-black St. George, and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Unity" title="Russian Unity">Russian Unity</a> party flags. Mayor Oleh Osadchy attempted to disperse the crowd and police eventually arrived to defend the flag. The mayor said "This is the territory of Ukraine, Crimea. Here's a flag of Crimea", but was accused of treason and a fight ensued over the flagpole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> On 24 February, more rallied outside the Sevastopol city state administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> Pro-Russian demonstrators accompanied by neo-Cossacks demanded the election of a Russian citizen as mayor and hoisted Russian flags around the city administration; they also handed out leaflets to sign up for a self-defence militia, warning that the "<a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">Blue</a>-<a href="/wiki/Sturmabteilung" title="Sturmabteilung">Brown</a> Europlague is knocking."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 February, several hundred pro-Russian protesters blocked the Crimean parliament demanding a referendum on Crimea's independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> On the same day, <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> illegally elected <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexei_Chaly" title="Alexei Chaly">Alexei Chaly</a>, a Russian citizen, as mayor. Under the law of Ukraine, it was not possible for Sevastopol to elect a mayor, as the <i>Chairman of the Sevastopol City State Administration</i>, appointed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ukraine" title="President of Ukraine">President of Ukraine</a>, functions as its mayor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YavlinskyUkr_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-YavlinskyUkr-95">[94]</a></sup> A thousand protesters present chanted "A Russian mayor for a Russian city." Crowds gathered again outside Sevastopol's city hall on Tuesday as rumours spread that security forces could arrest Chaly, but police chief Alexander Goncharov said that his officers would refuse to carry out "criminal orders" issued by Kiev. Viktor Neganov, a Sevastopol-based adviser to the Internal Affairs Minister, condemned the events in the city as a coup. "Chaly represents the interests of the Kremlin which likely gave its tacit approval," he said. Sevastopol City State Administration chairman Vladimir Yatsuba was booed and heckled on 23 February, when he told a pro-Russian rally that Crimea was part of Ukraine. He resigned the next day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> In Simferopol, the Regional State Administration building was blockaded with hundreds of protesters, including neo-Cossacks, demanding a referendum of separation; the rally was organized by the <i>Crimean Front</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 26 February, thousands clashed during opposing rallies in Simferopol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> Near the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_of_Crimea" title="Supreme Council of Crimea">Supreme Council of Crimea</a> building 4,000 and 5,000 <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatars" title="Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars</a> and supporters of the <a href="/wiki/Euromaidan" title="Euromaidan">Euromaidan</a>-Crimea movement faced 600-700 supporters of pro-Russian organizations and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Unity" title="Russian Unity">Russian Unity</a> Party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_of_Crimea" title="Supreme Council of Crimea">Supreme Council</a> Chairman <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Konstantinov" title="Vladimir Konstantinov">Vladimir Konstantinov</a> said that the Crimean parliament would not consider separation from Ukraine, and that earlier reports that parliament would hold a debate on the matter were provocations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> Tatars created self-defence groups, encouraged collaboration with Russians, Ukrainians, and people of other nationalities, and called for the protection of churches, mosques, synagogues, and other important sites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> By nightfall the Crimean Tatars had left; several hundred Russian Unity supporters rallied on.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Yatsenyuk_Government" title="First Yatsenyuk Government">new Ukrainian government</a>'s acting Internal Affairs Minister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arsen_Avakov_(politician)" title="Arsen Avakov (politician)">Arsen Avakov</a> tasked Crimean law enforcement agencies not to provoke conflicts and to do whatever necessary to prevent clashes with pro-Russian forces; and he added "I think, that way – through a dialogue – we shall achieve much more than with standoffs".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> New <a href="/wiki/Security_Service_of_Ukraine" title="Security Service of Ukraine">Security Service of Ukraine</a> (SBU) chief <a href="/wiki/Valentyn_Nalyvaichenko" title="Valentyn Nalyvaichenko">Valentyn Nalyvaichenko</a> requested that the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> provide around-the-clock monitoring of the security situation in Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> Russian troops took control of the main route to <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> on orders from Russian president <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>. A military checkpoint, with a Russian flag and Russian military vehicles, was set up on the main highway between the city and <a href="/wiki/Simferopol" title="Simferopol">Simferopol</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-globe26_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-globe26-105">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 27 February, <a href="/wiki/Spetsnaz" title="Spetsnaz">Russian special forces</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> seized the <a href="/wiki/Building_of_the_Supreme_Council_of_Crimea" title="Building of the Supreme Council of Crimea">building of the Supreme Council of Crimea</a> and the building of the Council of Ministers in <a href="/wiki/Simferopol" title="Simferopol">Simferopol</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Russia" title="Flag of Russia">Russian flags</a> were raised over these buildings,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Barricade" title="Barricade">barricades</a> were erected outside them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LentaBerkut_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-LentaBerkut-110">[109]</a></sup> Whilst the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Little_green_men_(GRU)" title="Little green men (GRU)">little green men</a>" were occupying the Crimean parliament building, the parliament held an emergency session.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interfax27feb_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-interfax27feb-111">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters13mar_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters13mar-112">[111]</a></sup> It voted to terminate the Crimean government, and replace Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Anatolii_Mohyliov" title="Anatolii Mohyliov">Anatolii Mohyliov</a> with <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Aksyonov" title="Sergey Aksyonov">Sergey Aksyonov</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Christian_Science_Monitor_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Christian_Science_Monitor-113">[112]</a></sup> Aksyonov belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Unity" title="Russian Unity">Russian Unity</a> party, which received 4% of the vote in the last election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters13mar_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-reuters13mar-112">[111]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ukraine" title="Constitution of Ukraine">Constitution of Ukraine</a>, the Prime Minister of Crimea is appointed by the Supreme Council of Crimea in consultation with the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ukraine" title="President of Ukraine">President of Ukraine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yanu.27snewPMC_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yanu.27snewPMC-114">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> Both Aksyonov and speaker Vladimir Konstantinov stated that they viewed Viktor Yanukovych as the <i>de jure</i> <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ukraine" title="President of Ukraine">president of Ukraine</a>, through whom they were able to ask Russia for assistance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>The parliament also voted to hold a referendum on greater autonomy on 25 May. The troops had cut all of the building's communications, and took MPs' phones as they entered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interfax27feb_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-interfax27feb-111">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters13mar_112-2"><a href="#cite_note-reuters13mar-112">[111]</a></sup> No independent journalists were allowed inside the building while the votes were taking place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters13mar_112-3"><a href="#cite_note-reuters13mar-112">[111]</a></sup> Some MPs said they were being threatened and that votes were cast for them and other MPs, even though they were not in the chamber.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters13mar_112-4"><a href="#cite_note-reuters13mar-112">[111]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Interfax-Ukraine" title="Interfax-Ukraine">Interfax-Ukraine</a> reported "it is impossible to find out whether all the 64 members of the 100-member legislature who were registered as present at when the two decisions were voted on or whether someone else used the plastic voting cards of some of them" because due to the armed occupation of parliament it was unclear how many MPs were present.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IUCR27214_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-IUCR27214-117">[116]</a></sup> The head of parliament's information and analysis department, Olha Sulnikova, had phoned from inside the <a href="/wiki/Building_of_the_Supreme_Council_of_Crimea" title="Building of the Supreme Council of Crimea">parliamentary building</a> to journalists and had told them 61 of the registered 64 deputies had voted for the referendum resolution and 55 for the resolution to dismiss the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IUCR27214_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-IUCR27214-117">[116]</a></sup> Donetsk People's Republic separatist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Igor_Girkin" title="Igor Girkin">Igor Girkin</a> said in January 2015 that Crimean members of parliament were held at gunpoint, and were forced to support the annexation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KP11MA2015_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-KP11MA2015-118">[117]</a></sup> These actions were immediately declared illegal by the Ukrainian interim government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the same day, more troops in unmarked uniforms, assisted this time by what appeared to be local <i><a href="/wiki/Berkut_(special_police_force)" title="Berkut (special police force)">Berkut</a></i> riot police (as well as Russian troops from the <a href="/wiki/31st_Guards_Air_Assault_Brigade" title="31st Guards Air Assault Brigade">31st Separate Airborne Assault Brigade</a> dressed in Berkut uniforms),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> established <a href="/wiki/Security_checkpoint" title="Security checkpoint">security checkpoints</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Perekop" title="Isthmus of Perekop">Isthmus of Perekop</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chonhar_Peninsula" title="Chonhar Peninsula">Chonhar Peninsula</a>, which separate Crimea from the Ukrainian mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LentaBerkut_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-LentaBerkut-110">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> Within hours, Ukraine had effectively been cut off from Crimea.</p>
<p>On 1 March 2014, Aksyonov declared Crimea's new <i>de facto</i> authorities would exercise control of all Ukrainian military installations on the peninsula. He also asked Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>, who had been Yanukovych's primary international backer and guarantor, for "assistance in ensuring peace and public order" in Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> Putin promptly received authorisation from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federation_Council_of_Russia" title="Federation Council of Russia">Federation Council of Russia</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Russian_military_intervention_in_Ukraine_(2014%E2%80%93present)" title="Russian military intervention in Ukraine (2014–present)">Russian military intervention in Ukraine</a> "until normalization of a socio-political environment in the country".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> Putin's swift manoeuvre prompted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protests_of_Russian_intelligentsia_against_the_annexation_of_Crimea" title="Protests of Russian intelligentsia against the annexation of Crimea">protests of intelligentsia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014_Russian_anti-war_protests" title="2014 Russian anti-war protests">demonstrations in Moscow</a> against a Russian military campaign in Crimea. By 2 March, Russian troops moving from the country's naval base in <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> and reinforced by troops, armour, and helicopters from mainland Russia exercised complete control over the Crimean Peninsula.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-walker-the-guardian-2014-descend_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-walker-the-guardian-2014-descend-129">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomberg-news-2014-request_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg-news-2014-request-130">[129]</a></sup> Russian troops operated in Crimea without insignia. On 4 March <a href="/wiki/General_Staff_of_the_Ukrainian_Armed_Forces" title="General Staff of the Ukrainian Armed Forces">Ukrainian General Staff</a> claimed there are units of <a href="/wiki/18th_Guards_Motor_Rifle_Brigade" title="18th Guards Motor Rifle Brigade">18th Motor Rifle Brigade</a>, <a href="/wiki/31st_Guards_Air_Assault_Brigade" title="31st Guards Air Assault Brigade">31st Air Assault Brigade</a> and <a href="/wiki/22nd_Spetsnaz_Brigade" title="22nd Spetsnaz Brigade">22nd Spetsnaz Brigade</a> deployed and operating in Crimea instead of <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Black Sea Fleet">Russian Black Sea Fleet</a> personnel, which violates international agreements signed by Ukraine and Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zsu_henshtab_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-zsu_henshtab-131">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zsu_interfax_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-zsu_interfax-132">[131]</a></sup> Despite numerous media reports and statements by the Ukrainian and foreign governments describing the unmarked troops as Russian soldiers, government officials <a href="/wiki/Military_deception" title="Military deception">concealed</a> the identity of their forces, claiming they were local "self-defence" units over whom they had no authority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> As late as 17 April, Russian foreign minister Lavrov said that there were no spare armed forces in the territory of Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>Russian officials eventually admitted to their troops' presence. On 17 April 2014, Putin acknowledged the Russian military backed Crimean separatist militias, stating that Russia's intervention was necessary "to ensure proper conditions for the people of Crimea to be able to freely express their will".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Putin17April_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Putin17April-32">[32]</a></sup> Defence Minister <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Shoygu" title="Sergey Shoygu">Sergey Shoygu</a> said the country's military actions in Crimea were undertaken by forces of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Black Sea Fleet">Black Sea Fleet</a> and were justified by "threat to lives of Crimean <a href="/wiki/Civilian" title="Civilian">civilians</a>" and danger of "takeover of Russian military infrastructure by <a href="/wiki/Extremism" title="Extremism">extremists</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> Ukraine complained that by increasing its troop presence in Crimea, Russia violated the agreement under which it headquartered its Black Sea Fleet in Sevastopol<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> and violated the country's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independence_of_Ukraine" title="Independence of Ukraine">sovereignty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blogs.telegraph.co.uk_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-blogs.telegraph.co.uk-137">[136]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> also accused Russia of breaking the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Budapest_Memorandum_on_Security_Assurances" title="Budapest Memorandum on Security Assurances">Budapest Memorandum on Security Assurances</a>, by which Russia, the US, and the UK had reaffirmed their obligation to refrain from the threat or use of force against the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_integrity" title="Territorial integrity">territorial integrity</a> or political independence of Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> The Russian government said the Budapest Memorandum did not apply due to "complicated internal processes" in Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> In March 2015 retired Russian Admiral Igor Kasatonov stated that according to his information the Russian troop deployment in Crimea included six helicopter landings and three landings of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IL-76" title="IL-76">IL-76</a> with 500 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_obstacles_to_Crimea_annexation">Legal obstacles to Crimea annexation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Legal obstacles to Crimea annexation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_of_Crimea" title="Declaration of Independence of Crimea">Declaration of Independence of Crimea</a></div>

<p>The Russian–Ukrainian <a href="/wiki/Partition_Treaty_on_the_Status_and_Conditions_of_the_Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Partition Treaty on the Status and Conditions of the Black Sea Fleet">Partition Treaty on the Status and Conditions of the Black Sea Fleet</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[a]</a></sup> signed in 1997 and prolonged in 2010, determined the status of the military bases and vessels in Crimea prior to the crisis. Russia was allowed to maintain up to 25,000 troops, 24 artillery systems (with a calibre smaller than 100 mm), 132 armoured vehicles, and 22 military planes, on military base in Sevastopol and related infrastructure on the Crimean Peninsula. The Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Sea_fleet" title="Black Sea fleet">Black Sea fleet</a> had basing rights in <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a> until 2042. Usage of navigation stations and troop movements were improperly covered by the treaty and were violated many times as well as related court decisions. February troop movements were in "complete disregard" of the treaty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yeroshko_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yeroshko-144">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Both Russia and Ukraine are signatories to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_United_Nations" title="Charter of the United Nations">Charter of the United Nations</a>. The ratification of said charter has several ramifications in terms of <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>, particularly those that cover the subjects of <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice_advisory_opinion_on_Kosovo%27s_declaration_of_independence" title="International Court of Justice advisory opinion on Kosovo's declaration of independence">declarations of independence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">self-determination</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acts_of_aggression" title="Acts of aggression">acts of aggression</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_aid" title="Humanitarian aid">humanitarian emergencies</a>. <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> said that Russian troops in the Crimean peninsula were aimed "to ensure proper conditions for the people of Crimea to be able to freely express their will",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> whilst Ukraine and other nations argue that such intervention is a violation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independence_of_Ukraine" title="Independence of Ukraine">Ukraine's sovereignty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blogs.telegraph.co.uk_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-blogs.telegraph.co.uk-137">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>Russia, United States, United Kingdom and Ukraine also signed the <a href="/wiki/Budapest_Memorandum_on_Security_Assurances" title="Budapest Memorandum on Security Assurances">Budapest Memorandum on Security Assurances</a>, by which all these countries reaffirmed their obligation to respect the territorial integrity of Ukraine (including Crimea) and to refrain from the threat or use of force against the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_integrity" title="Territorial integrity">territorial integrity</a> or political independence of Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2014-03-09_-_Perevalne_military_base_-_0162.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="4608" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/2014-03-09_-_Perevalne_military_base_-_0162.JPG/250px-2014-03-09_-_Perevalne_military_base_-_0162.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/2014-03-09_-_Perevalne_military_base_-_0162.JPG/375px-2014-03-09_-_Perevalne_military_base_-_0162.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/2014-03-09_-_Perevalne_military_base_-_0162.JPG/500px-2014-03-09_-_Perevalne_military_base_-_0162.JPG 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2014-03-09_-_Perevalne_military_base_-_0162.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"<a href="/wiki/Little_green_men_(Ukrainian_crisis)" title="Little green men (Ukrainian crisis)">Little green men</a>" and lorries after the seizure of <a href="/wiki/Perevalne" title="Perevalne">Perevalne</a> military base, 9 March 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><span id="Declaration_of_Independence:_a_letter_of_intent"></span>According to the Constitution of Russia, the admission of new federal subjects is governed by federal constitutional law (art. 65.2).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup> Such a law was adopted in 2001, and it postulates that admission of a foreign state or its part into Russia shall be based on a mutual accord between the Russian Federation and the relevant state and shall take place pursuant to an international treaty between the two countries; moreover, it must be initiated by the state in question, not by its subdivision or by Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 28 February 2014, Russian MP <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Mironov" title="Sergey Mironov">Sergey Mironov</a>, along with other members of the Duma, introduced a bill to alter Russia's procedure for adding federal subjects. According to the bill, accession could be initiated by a subdivision of a country, provided that there is "absence of efficient sovereign state government in foreign state"; the request could be made either by subdivision bodies on their own or on the basis of a referendum held in the subdivision in accordance with corresponding national legislation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 March 2014, both the Supreme Council of Crimea and the Sevastopol City Council adopted a <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_of_the_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Declaration of Independence of the Republic of Crimea">declaration of independence</a>, which stated their intent to declare independence and request full accession to Russia should the pro-Russian option receive the most votes during the scheduled status referendum. The declaration directly referred to the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_independence_precedent" title="Kosovo independence precedent">Kosovo independence precedent</a>, by which the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albanian_people" title="Albanian people">Albanian</a>-populated <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija</a> declared independence from Russia's ally <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Kosovo" title="Republic of Kosovo">Republic of Kosovo</a> in 2008—a unilateral action Russia <a href="/wiki/Russia%27s_reaction_to_the_2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="Russia's reaction to the 2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">staunchly opposed</a>. Many analysts saw the Crimean declaration as an overt effort to pave the way for Crimea's annexation by Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>Crimean authorities' stated plans to declare independence from Ukraine made the Mironov bill unnecessary. On 20 March 2014, two days after the <a href="#Admission_treaty_and_aftermath">treaty of accession</a> was signed, the bill was withdrawn by its initiators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>At its meeting on 21–22 March, the <a href="/wiki/Venice_Commission" title="Venice Commission">Venice Commission</a> stated that the Mironov bill violated "in particular, the principles of territorial integrity, national sovereignty, non-intervention in the internal affairs of another state and <a href="/wiki/Pacta_sunt_servanda" title="Pacta sunt servanda">pacta sunt servanda</a>" and was therefore incompatible with <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crimean_status_referendum">Crimean status referendum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Crimean status referendum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Crimean_status_referendum,_2014" title="Crimean status referendum, 2014">Crimean status referendum, 2014</a></div>
<p>On 27 February, following the takeover of its building by Russian special forces, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_of_Crimea" title="Supreme Council of Crimea">Supreme Council of Crimea</a> voted to hold a <a href="/wiki/Crimean_status_referendum,_2014" title="Crimean status referendum, 2014">referendum</a> on 25 May, with the initial question as to whether Crimea should upgrade its autonomy within Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup> The referendum date was later moved from 25 May to 30 March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup> A Ukrainian court declared the referendum to be illegal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 March, Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> said Russia was not considering annexing Crimea. He said of the peninsula that "only citizens themselves, in conditions of free expression of will and their security can determine their future".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> Putin later acknowledged that he had ordered "work to bring Crimea back into Russia" as early as February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup> He also acknowledged that in early March there were "secret opinion polls" held in Crimea, which, according to him, reported overwhelming popular support for Crimea's incorporation into Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 March, the Supreme Council moved the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimean_referendum,_2014" title="Crimean referendum, 2014">referendum</a> date to 16 March and changed its scope to ask a new question: whether Crimea should accede to Russia or restore the 1992 constitution within Ukraine, which the Ukrainian government had previously invalidated. This referendum, unlike one announced earlier, contained no option to maintain the <i>status quo</i> of governance under the 1998 constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> Ukraine's then-acting President, Oleksander Turchinov, stated that "The authorities in Crimea are totally illegitimate, both the parliament and the government. They are forced to work under the barrel of a gun and all their decisions are dictated by fear and are illegal."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reutersgun_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-reutersgun-160">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 March, the Crimean status referendum was deemed unconstitutional by the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Ukraine" title="Constitutional Court of Ukraine">Constitutional Court of Ukraine</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup> and a day later, the <a href="/wiki/Verkhovna_Rada" title="Verkhovna Rada">Verkhovna Rada</a> formally dissolved the Crimean parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zakon_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-zakon-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>The referendum was held despite the opposition from the Ukrainian government. Official results reported about 95% of participating voters in Crimea were in favour of Russian annexation of Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup> The results of referendum were questioned;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup> another report by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Evgeny_Bobrov&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Evgeny Bobrov (page does not exist)">Evgeny Bobrov</a>, a member of the Russian President's Human Rights Council, suggested the official results were inflated and only 15% to 30% of Crimeans eligible to vote actually voted for the Russian option.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Washington_Post_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Washington_Post-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>The means by which the referendum was conducted were widely criticised by foreign governments and in the Ukrainian and international press, with reports that anyone holding a Russian passport regardless of residency in Crimea was allowed to vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fast_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-fast-165">[163]</a></sup> After the OSCE refused to send observers Russia invited a group of observers from various European <a href="/wiki/Far-right_politics" title="Far-right politics">far-right</a> political parties aligned with Putin, who stated the referendum was conducted in a free and fair manner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Breakaway_republic">Breakaway republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Breakaway republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_of_the_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Declaration of Independence of the Republic of Crimea">Declaration of Independence of the Republic of Crimea</a></div>
<p>On 17 March, following the official announcement of the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_status_referendum,_2014" title="Crimean status referendum, 2014">referendum</a> results, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_of_Crimea" title="Supreme Council of Crimea">Supreme Council of Crimea</a> declared the formal independence of the <b>Republic of Crimea</b>, comprising the territories of both the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Autonomous Republic of Crimea">Autonomous Republic of Crimea</a> and the city of <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a>, which was granted special status within the breakaway republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-res1745_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-res1745-168">[166]</a></sup> The Crimean parliament declared the "partial repeal" of Ukrainian laws and began nationalising private and Ukrainian state property located on the Crimean Peninsula, including Ukrainian <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">ports</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[167]</a></sup> and property of <a href="/wiki/Chornomornaftogaz" title="Chornomornaftogaz">Chornomornaftogaz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup> Parliament also formally requested that the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Russia" title="Government of Russia">Russian government</a> admit the breakaway republic into Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian20140317_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian20140317-171">[169]</a></sup> On same day, the <i>de facto</i> Supreme Council renamed itself the Crimean State Council,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup> declared the <a href="/wiki/Russian_ruble" title="Russian ruble">Russian ruble</a> an official currency alongside the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_hryvnia" title="Ukrainian hryvnia">hryvnia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup> and announced that Crimea would switch to <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Time" title="Moscow Time">Moscow Time</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC%2B4:00" title="UTC+4:00">UTC+4</a>) on 30 March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup></p>
<p>Putin officially recognised the Republic of Crimea 'as a sovereign and independent state' by <a href="/wiki/Decree_of_the_President_of_Russia" title="Decree of the President of Russia">decree</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup> and approved the admission of Crimea and Sevastopol as <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia" title="Federal subjects of Russia">federal subjects of Russia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accession_treaty">Accession treaty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Accession treaty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
