<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C_%C2%AB%D0%97%D0%B0_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B2%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%9A%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BC%D0%B0%C2%BB_%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Medal "For return of Crimea" (20 February 2014 – 18 March 2014) by the Ministry of Defense of Russia</div>

</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Federal_District" title="Crimean Federal District">Crimean Federal District</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Crimea" title="Political status of Crimea">Political status of Crimea</a></div>
<p>The Treaty on Accession of the Republic of Crimea to Russia was signed between representatives of the Republic of Crimea (including Sevastopol, with which the rest of Crimea briefly unified) and the Russian Federation on 18 March 2014 to lay out terms for the immediate admission of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> as <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia" title="Federal subjects of Russia">federal subjects of Russia</a> and part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup> It was ratified by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Assembly_(Russia)" title="Federal Assembly (Russia)">Federal Assembly</a> by 21 March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>During <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Simferopol_incident" title="Simferopol incident">a controversial incident in Simferopol</a> on 18 March, some Ukrainian sources said that armed gunmen that were reported to be Russian special forces allegedly stormed the base. This was contested by Russian authorities, who subsequently arrested an alleged Ukrainian sniper in connection with the killings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>The two casualties had a joint funeral attended by both the Crimean and Ukrainian authorities, and both soldiers were mourned together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup> The incident is now under investigation by both the Crimean authorities and the Ukrainian military.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 19 March, President Putin submitted a treaty on Crimea's annexation by Russia and a constitutional amendment to set up two new federal subjects of the Russian Federation to the <a href="/wiki/State_Duma" title="State Duma">State Duma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup> The Russian Constitutional Court found that treaty is in compliance with the Constitution of Russia. The court sat in an emergency session following a formal request by President Vladimir Putin to assess the constitutionality of the treaty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[184]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the Russian Constitutional Court upheld the constitutionality of the treaty, the State Duma ratified it on 20 March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup> The Duma also approved the draft federal constitutional law admitting Crimea and Sevastopol and establishing them as federal subjects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[189]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/A_Just_Russia" title="A Just Russia">A Just Russia</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ilya_Ponomarev" title="Ilya Ponomarev">Ilya Ponomarev</a> was the only State Duma member to vote against the measures. A day later, the treaty itself and the required amendment to article 65 of the Russian Constitution (which lists the <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia" title="Federal subjects of Russia">federal subjects of Russia</a>) were ratified by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federation_Council" title="Federation Council">Federation Council</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[190]</a></sup> and almost immediately signed into law by Putin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup> Crimea's admission to the Russian Federation was considered retroactive to 18 March, when Putin and Crimean leaders signed the draft treaty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[192]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsequent_events">Subsequent events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Subsequent events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-Prose" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>contains <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Embedded_lists" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Embedded lists">embedded lists</a> that may be better presented using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Prose" title="Wikipedia:Prose">prose</a>.</b> <span class="hide-when-compact">You can help by converting the list or lists to prose, if <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Embedded_lists" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Embedded lists">appropriate</a>. <a href="/wiki/Help:Editing" title="Help:Editing">Editing help</a> is available.</span> <small><i>(March 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On 24 March, the Ukrainian government ordered the full withdrawal of all of its armed forces from Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup> In addition, the Ministry of Defence announced that approximately 50% of the Ukrainian soldiers in Crimea had defected to the Russian military.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 27 March, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> adopted a <a href="/wiki/Non-binding_resolution" title="Non-binding resolution">non-binding</a> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_68/262" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 68/262">resolution</a>, which declared the Crimean referendum and subsequent status change invalid, by a vote of 100 to 11, with 58 abstentions and 24 absent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[198]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[199]</a></sup></p>
<p>Crimea and Sevastopol switched to <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Time" title="Moscow Time">Moscow Time</a> at the end of March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crimean_time_change_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-Crimean_time_change-202">[200]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time_switch_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-Time_switch-203">[201]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 2 April, Russia formally <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denunciation_(international_law)" title="Denunciation (international law)">denounced</a> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_Kharkiv_Pact" title="2010 Kharkiv Pact">2010 Kharkiv Pact</a> and <a href="/wiki/Partition_Treaty_on_the_Status_and_Conditions_of_the_Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Partition Treaty on the Status and Conditions of the Black Sea Fleet">Partition Treaty on the Status and Conditions of the Black Sea Fleet</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[202]</a></sup> Putin cited "the accession of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a> and Sevastopol into Russia" and resulting "practical end of <a href="/wiki/Renting" title="Renting">renting</a> relationships" as his reason for the denunciation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[203]</a></sup> On the same day, he signed a decree formally rehabilitating the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatars" title="Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars</a>, who were <a href="/wiki/Deportation_of_the_Crimean_Tatars" title="Deportation of the Crimean Tatars">ousted from their lands</a> in 1944, and the Armenian, German, Greek, and Bulgarian minority communities in the region that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Josef_Stalin" title="Josef Stalin">Stalin</a> also ordered removed in the 1940s.</p>
<p>On 11 April, the Constitution of the Republic of Crimea and City Charter of Sevastopol were adopted,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[204]</a></sup> in addition the new federal subjects were enumerated in a newly published revision of the Russian Constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[205]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">

</div>
</div>
<p>On 14 April, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> announced that he would open a ruble-only account with <a href="/wiki/Rossiya_Bank" title="Rossiya Bank">Bank Rossiya</a> and would make it the primary bank in the newly annexed Crimea as well as giving the right to service payments on Russia's $36 billion wholesale electricity market – which gave the bank $112 million annually from commission charges alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[206]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2015, Russian Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a>, declared that Crimea had been fully integrated into Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[207]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2016_Crimea_border_clashes">2016 Crimea border clashes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2016 Crimea border clashes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 8 August 2016, Ukraine reported that Russia had increased its military presence along the demarcation line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[208]</a></sup> In response to this military buildup Ukraine also deployed more troops and resources closer to the border with Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[209]</a></sup> The Pentagon has downplayed a Russian invasion of Ukraine, calling Russian troops along the border a regular military exercise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[210]</a></sup> On 10 August, Russia claimed two servicemen were killed in clashes with Ukrainian commandos, and that Ukrainian servicemen had been captured with a total of 40 kg of explosives in their possession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[211]</a></sup> Ukraine denied that the incident took place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[212]</a></sup> Russian accounts claimed that Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FSB_(Russia)" title="FSB (Russia)">FSB</a> detained "Ukrainian saboteurs" and "terrorists" near Armyansk. The ensuing gunfight left one FSB officer and a suspect dead. A number of individuals were detained, including Yevhen Panov, who is described by Russian sources as a Ukrainian military intelligence officer and leader of the sabotage group. The group was allegedly planning terror attacks on important infrastructure in Armyansk, Crimea. Ukrainian media reported that Panov was a military volunteer fighting in the east of the country, however he has more recently been associated with a charitable organization. Russia also claimed that the alleged border infiltration was accompanied by "heavy fire" from Ukrainian territory, resulting in the death of a Russian soldier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[213]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[214]</a></sup> Ukrainian government called the Russian accusations "cynical" and "senseless" and argued that since Crimea was Ukrainian territory, it was Russia which "has been generously financing and actively supporting terrorism on Ukrainian territory".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[215]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transition_and_aftermath">Transition and aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Transition and aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_implications">Economic implications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economic implications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The number of tourists visiting Crimea in the 2014 season was lower than in the previous years due to a combination of <a href="/wiki/International_sanctions_during_the_Ukrainian_crisis" title="International sanctions during the Ukrainian crisis">Western sanctions</a>, ethical objections by Ukrainians, and the difficulty of getting there for Russians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[216]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[217]</a></sup> The Russian government attempted to stimulate the flow of tourists by subsidizing holidays in the peninsula for children and state workers from all Russia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[218]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[219]</a></sup> which worked mostly for state-owned hotels. In 2015 overall 3 million tourists visited Crimea according to official data, while before annexation it was around 5.5 million on average. The shortage is attributed mostly to stopped flow of tourists from Ukraine. Hotels and restaurants are also experiencing problems with finding enough seasonal workers, who were arriving from Ukraine mostly in the preceding years. Tourists visiting state-owned hotels are complaining mostly about low standard of rooms and facilities, some of them unrepaired from Soviet times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[220]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the German newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Welt" title="Die Welt">Die Welt</a></i>, the annexation of Crimea is economically disadvantageous for the Russian Federation. Russia will have to spend billions of euros a year to pay salaries and pensions. Moreover, Russia will have to undertake costly projects to connect Crimea to the Russian water supply and power system because Crimea has no land connection to Russia and at present gets water, gas and electricity from mainland Ukraine. This will require building <a href="/wiki/Kerch_Strait_Bridge" title="Kerch Strait Bridge">a bridge</a> and a pipeline across the <a href="/wiki/Kerch_Strait" title="Kerch Strait">Kerch Strait</a>. Also, Novinite claims that a Ukrainian expert told <i>Die Welt</i> that Crimea "will not be able to attract tourists".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[221]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first Deputy to <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Finance_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Finance (Russia)">Minister of Finance</a> of Russian Federation Tatyana Nesterenko said in her interview to <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a> Woman</i> that decision to annexe Crimea was made by Russian President Vladimir Putin exclusively without consulting Russia's Finance Ministry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[222]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Russian <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Russia" title="Media of Russia">business newspaper</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Kommersant" title="Kommersant">Kommersant</a></i> expresses an opinion that Russia will not acquire anything economically from "accessing" Crimea, which is not very developed industrially, having just a few big factories, and whose yearly gross product is only $4 billion. The newspaper also says that everything from Russia will have to be delivered by sea, higher costs of transportation will result in higher prices for everything, and to avoid a decline in living standards Russia will have to subsidise Crimean people for a few months. In total, Kommersant estimates the costs of integrating Crimea into Russia in $30 billion over the next decade, i.e. $3 billion per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kommersant20140207_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-kommersant20140207-225">[223]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the other hand, western oil experts estimate that Russia's seizing of Crimea, and the associated control of an area of Black Sea more than three times its land area gives it access to oil and gas reserves potentially worth trillions of dollars. It also deprives Ukraine of its chances of energy independence. Most immediately however, analysts say, Moscow's acquisition may alter the route along which the <a href="/wiki/South_Stream" title="South Stream">South Stream</a> pipeline would be built, saving Russia money, time and engineering challenges. It would also allow Russia to avoid building in Turkish territorial waters, which was necessary in the original route to avoid Ukrainian territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-In_taking_Crimea.2C_Putin_gains_a_sea_of_fuel_reserves_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-In_taking_Crimea.2C_Putin_gains_a_sea_of_fuel_reserves-226">[224]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[225]</a></sup></p>
<p>Russian/<a href="/wiki/Chechnya" title="Chechnya">Chechen</a> businessman <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ruslan_Baisarov&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ruslan Baisarov (page does not exist)">Ruslan Baisarov</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%91%D0%B0%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2,_%D0%A0%D1%83%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87" title="ru:Байсаров, Руслан Сулимович">ru</a>)</span> announced he is ready to invest 12 billion rubles into the construction of a modern sea resort in Crimea, which is expected to create about 1,300 jobs. <a href="/wiki/Ramzan_Kadyrov" title="Ramzan Kadyrov">Ramzan Kadyrov</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_the_Chechen_Republic" title="Head of the Chechen Republic">Head of Chechnya</a>, said that other Chechen businessmen are planning to invest into Crimea as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[226]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Service_for_Supervision_of_Communications,_Information_Technology_and_Mass_Media" title="Federal Service for Supervision of Communications, Information Technology and Mass Media">Russian Federal Service for Communications</a> (Roskomnadzor) warned about a transition period as Russian operators have to change the numbering capacity and subscribers. <a href="/wiki/Country_code" title="Country code">Country code</a> will be replaced from the <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_Ukraine" title="Telephone numbers in Ukraine">Ukrainian +380</a> to <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_Russia" title="Telephone numbers in Russia">Russian +7</a>. Codes in Crimea start with <a href="/wiki/List_of_dialling_codes_in_Ukraine#65_.E2.80.93_Crimea" title="List of dialling codes in Ukraine">65</a>, but in the area of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_Soviet_Union" title="Telephone numbers in Soviet Union">"7"</a> the 6 is given to Kazakhstan which shares former Soviet Union +7 with Russia, so city codes have to change. The regulator assigned 869 <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_Russia" title="Telephone numbers in Russia">dialling code</a> to Sevastopol and the rest of the peninsula received a 365 code.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[227]</a></sup> At the time of the unification with Russia, telephone operators and Internet service providers in Crimea and Sevastopol are connected to the outside world through the territory of Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[228]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Communications_and_Mass_Media_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Communications and Mass Media (Russia)">Minister of Communications</a> of Russia, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nikolai_Nikiforov" title="Nikolai Nikiforov">Nikolai Nikiforov</a> announced on his <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> account that <a href="/wiki/Postal_codes_in_Russia" title="Postal codes in Russia">postal codes</a> in Crimea will now have six-figures: to the existing five-digit number the number two will be added at the beginning. For example, the Simferopol postal code 95000 will become 295000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[229]</a></sup></p>
<p>Regarding Crimea's borders, the head of Russian Federal Agency for the Development of the State Border Facilities (Rosgranitsa) Konstantin Busygin, who was speaking at a meeting led by Russian Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Rogozin" title="Dmitry Rogozin">Dmitry Rogozin</a> in <a href="/wiki/Simferopol" title="Simferopol">Simferopol</a>, the capital of Crimea said the <a href="/wiki/Borders_of_Russia" title="Borders of Russia">Russian state border</a> in the north of Crimea which, according to his claims, now forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Russia%E2%80%93Ukraine_border" title="Russia–Ukraine border">Russian-Ukrainian border</a>, will be fully equipped with the necessary facilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[230]</a></sup> In the area that now forms the border between Crimea and Ukraine mining the salt lake inlets from the sea that constitute the natural borders, and in the spit of land left over stretches of no-man's-land with wire on either side was created.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[231]</a></sup> On early June that year <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Russia" title="Prime Minister of Russia">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a> signed a <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Government_of_Russia" title="Order of the Government of Russia">Government resolution</a> №961<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[232]</a></sup> dated 5 June 2014 establishing air, sea, road and railway checkpoints. The adopted decisions create a legal basis for the functioning of a checkpoint system at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_state_border" title="Russian state border">Russian state border</a> in the Republic of Crimea and Sevastopol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[233]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the year following the annexation, armed men seized various Crimean businesses, including banks, hotels, shipyards, farms, gas stations, a <a href="/wiki/Bakery" title="Bakery">bakery</a>, a dairy, and Yalta Film Studio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP141202_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-AP141202-236">[234]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT150110_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT150110-237">[235]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP150227_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-AFP150227-238">[236]</a></sup> Russian media have noted this trend as "returning to the 90's", which is perceived as a period of anarchy and rule of gangs in Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[237]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015 the Investigative Committee of Russia announced about a number of theft and corruption cases in infrastructure projects in Crimea, for example spending that exceeded the actual accounted costs three times. A number of Russian officials were also arrested for corruption, including head of federal tax inspection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[239]</a></sup></p>
<p>(According to February 2016 official Ukrainian figures) after Russia's annexation 10% of <a href="/wiki/Security_Service_of_Ukraine" title="Security Service of Ukraine">Security Service of Ukraine</a> personnel left Crimea; accompanied by 6.000 of the pre-annexation 20.300 people strong <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_army" title="Ukrainian army">Ukrainian army</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[240]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights_situation">Human rights situation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Human rights situation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 2014, <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> reported that pro-Ukrainian activists and journalists had been attacked, abducted, and tortured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HRW140314_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-HRW140314-243">[241]</a></sup> Some Crimeans were simply "disappeared" with no explanation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-News_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-News-244">[242]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 9 May 2014 the new "anti-extremist" amendment to the <a href="/wiki/Criminal_Code_of_Russia" title="Criminal Code of Russia">Criminal Code of Russia</a>, passed in December 2013, came into force. Article 280.1 designated incitement of violation of territorial integrity of the Russian Federation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKRF280-1_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-UKRF280-1-245">[243]</a></sup> (incl. calls for secession of Crimea from Russia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[244]</a></sup>) as a criminal offense in Russia, punishable by a fine of 300 thousand roubles or imprisonment up to 3 years. If such statements are made in public media or the internet, the punishment could be obligatory works up to 480 hours or imprisonment up to five years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKRF280-1_245-1"><a href="#cite_note-UKRF280-1-245">[243]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the annexation of Crimea, according to report released on the Russian government run President of Russia's Council on Civil Society and Human Rights website, Tatars who were opposed to Russian rule have been persecuted, Russian law restricting freedom of speech has been imposed, and the new pro-Russian authorities "liquidated" the Kiev Patriarchate Orthodox church on the peninsula.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Washington_Post_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-Washington_Post-37">[37]</a></sup> The Crimean Tatar television station was also shut down by the Russian authorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-News_244-1"><a href="#cite_note-News-244">[242]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ukraine_census_2001_Russian.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="477" data-file-width="621" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ukraine_census_2001_Russian.svg/250px-Ukraine_census_2001_Russian.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ukraine_census_2001_Russian.svg/375px-Ukraine_census_2001_Russian.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ukraine_census_2001_Russian.svg/500px-Ukraine_census_2001_Russian.svg.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ukraine_census_2001_Russian.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map denoting the subdivisions of Ukraine and the percentage of people that indicated <a href="/wiki/Russian_language_in_Ukraine" title="Russian language in Ukraine">Russian</a> as their native language in the latest local census. <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> identifies itself as the highest at 90.6% followed immediately by Crimea at 77.0%.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the annexation, on 16 May the new Russian authorities of Crimea issued a ban on the annual commemorations of the anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Deportation_of_the_Crimean_Tatars" title="Deportation of the Crimean Tatars">Deportation of the Crimean Tatars</a> by Stalin in 1944, citing "possibility of provocation by extremists" as a reason.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[245]</a></sup> Previously, when Crimea was controlled by Ukraine, these commemorations had taken place every year. The pro-Russian Crimean authorities also banned <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Dzhemilev" title="Mustafa Dzhemilev">Mustafa Dzhemilev</a>, a human rights activist, Soviet dissident, member of the Ukrainian parliament, and former Chairman of the Mejlis of the Crimean Tatars from entering Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ft_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-ft-248">[246]</a></sup> Additionally, Mejlis reported, that officers of Russia's <a href="/wiki/Federal_Security_Service" title="Federal Security Service">Federal Security Service</a> (FSB) raided Tatar homes in the same week, on the pretense of "suspicion of terrorist activity".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reut_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-reut-249">[247]</a></sup> The Tatar community eventually did hold commemorative rallies in defiance of the ban.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ft_248-1"><a href="#cite_note-ft-248">[246]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reut_249-1"><a href="#cite_note-reut-249">[247]</a></sup> In response Russian authorities flew helicopters over the rallies in an attempt to disrupt them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc2_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc2-250">[248]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2015, a local activist, Alexander Kostenko, was sentenced to four years in a penal colony. His lawyer, Dmitry Sotnikov, said that the case was fabricated and that his client had been beaten and starved. Crimean prosecutor <a href="/wiki/Natalia_Poklonskaya" title="Natalia Poklonskaya">Natalia Poklonskaya</a> announced that they were judging "not just [Kostenko], but the very idea of fascism and nazism, which are trying to raise their head once again." Sotnikov responded that "There are fabricated cases in Russia, but rarely such humiliation and physical harm. A living person is being tortured for a political idea, to be able to boast winning over fascism."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP150515_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-AFP150515-251">[249]</a></sup> In June 2015, <a href="/wiki/Razom" title="Razom">Razom</a> released a report compiling human rights abuses in Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Razom150615_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-Razom150615-252">[250]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DB150623_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-DB150623-253">[251]</a></sup> In its 2016 annual report, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> made no mention of human rights abuses in Crimea because Russia had not allowed its monitors to enter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KP160621_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-KP160621-254">[252]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crimean_public_opinion">Crimean public opinion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Crimean public opinion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A joint survey by American government agency <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_Board_of_Governors" title="Broadcasting Board of Governors">Broadcasting Board of Governors</a> and polling firm <a href="/wiki/Gallup_(company)" title="Gallup (company)">Gallup</a> was taken during April 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FFS6464_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-FFS6464-255">[253]</a></sup> It polled 500 residents of Crimea. The survey found that 82.8% of those polled believed that the results of the Crimean status referendum reflected the views of most Crimeans, whereas 6.7% said that it did not. 73.9% of those polled said that they thought that the annexation would have a positive impact on their lives, whereas 5.5% said that it would not. 13.6% said that they did not know.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FFS6464_255-1"><a href="#cite_note-FFS6464-255">[253]</a></sup></p>
<p>A comprehensive poll released on 8 May 2014 by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Centre" title="Pew Research Centre">Pew Research Centre</a> surveyed Crimean opinions on the annexation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PewReport_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-PewReport-256">[254]</a></sup> Despite international criticism of 16 March <a href="/wiki/Crimean_status_referendum,_2014" title="Crimean status referendum, 2014">referendum on Crimean status</a>, 91% of those Crimeans polled thought that the vote was free and fair, and 88% said that the Ukrainian government should recognise the results.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PewReport_256-1"><a href="#cite_note-PewReport-256">[254]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ukrainian_response">Ukrainian response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ukrainian response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Do_not_buy_Russian_goods!" title="Do not buy Russian goods!">Do not buy Russian goods!</a> and <a href="/wiki/Putin_khuilo!" title="Putin khuilo!">Putin khuilo!</a></div>
<p>Immediately after the treaty of accession was signed in March, the Ukrainian Ministry of Foreign Affairs summoned the Provisional Principal of Russia in Ukraine to present <i><a href="/wiki/Note_verbale" title="Note verbale">note verbale</a></i> of protest against Russia's recognition of the Republic of Crimea and its subsequent annexation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[255]</a></sup> Two days later, the <a href="/wiki/Verkhovna_Rada" title="Verkhovna Rada">Verkhovna Rada</a> condemned the treaty<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[256]</a></sup> and called Russia's actions "a gross violation of <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>". The Rada called on the international community to avoid recognition of the "so-called Republic of Crimea" or the annexation of Crimea and Sevastopol by Russia as new federal subjects.</p>
<p>On 15 April 2014, the Verkhovna Rada declared the Autonomous Republic of Crimea and Sevastopol to be under "provisional <a href="/wiki/Military_occupation" title="Military occupation">occupation</a>" by the Russian military<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[257]</a></sup> and imposed <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_movement" title="Freedom of movement">travel restrictions</a> on Ukrainians visiting Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apr15_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-apr15-260">[258]</a></sup> The territories were also deemed "inalienable parts of Ukraine" subject to Ukrainian law. Among other things, the special law approved by the Rada restricted foreign citizens' movements to and from the Crimean Peninsula and forbade certain types of entrepreneurship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[259]</a></sup> The law also forbade activity of government bodies formed in violation of Ukrainian law and designated their acts as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Null_and_void" title="Null and void">null and void</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[260]</a></sup> The law had little to no actual effect in Crimea itself due to the mutual non-recognition between Kiev and Simferopol.</p>
<p>Ukrainian authorities greatly reduced the volume of <a href="/wiki/Canals_in_Ukraine" title="Canals in Ukraine">water flowing into Crimea</a> via the <a href="/wiki/North_Crimean_Canal" title="North Crimean Canal">North Crimean Canal</a> due to huge debt for water supplied in previous year, threatening the viability of the peninsula's agricultural crops, which are heavily dependent on irrigation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[261]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Ukrainian National Council for TV and Radio Broadcasting has instructed all cable operators on 11 March to stop transmitting a number of Russian channels, including the international versions of the main state-controlled stations, <a href="/wiki/Russia-1" title="Russia-1">Rossiya-1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Channel_One_Russia" title="Channel One Russia">Channel One</a> and NTV, as well as news channel <a href="/wiki/Russia-24" title="Russia-24">Rossiya-cable operators on</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[262]</a></sup> They said that this is because of Russian media showing them in a negative light.</p>
<p>In March 2014, activists began organising <a href="/wiki/Flash_mob" title="Flash mob">flash mobs</a> in supermarkets to urge customers <a href="/wiki/Do_not_buy_Russian_goods!" title="Do not buy Russian goods!">not to buy Russian goods</a> and to boycott Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gas_stations" title="Gas stations">gas stations</a>, banks, and concerts. In April 2014, some <a href="/wiki/Movie_theater" title="Movie theater">cinemas</a> in Kiev, Lviv, and Odessa began <a href="/wiki/Boycott_Russian_Films" title="Boycott Russian Films">shunning Russian films</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[263]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 2 December 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Information_Policy_(Ukraine)" title="Ministry of Information Policy (Ukraine)">Ministry of Information Policy</a> was created with one of its goals being, according to first Minister of Information, <a href="/wiki/Yuriy_Stets" title="Yuriy Stets">Yuriy Stets</a>, to counteract "Russian information aggression".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[264]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2014, Ukraine halted all train and bus services to Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[265]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 16 September 2015 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_parliament" title="Ukrainian parliament">Ukrainian parliament</a> voted for the law that sets 20 February 2014 as the official date of the Russian temporary occupation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimean_peninsula" title="Crimean peninsula">Crimean peninsula</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[266]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[267]</a></sup> On 7 October 2015 the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ukraine" title="President of Ukraine">President of Ukraine</a> signed the law into force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[268]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Temporarily_Occupied_Territories_and_IDPs" title="Ministry of Temporarily Occupied Territories and IDPs">Ministry of Temporarily Occupied Territories and IDPs</a> was established by Ukrainian government on 20 April 2016 to manage occupied parts of <a href="/wiki/Temporarily_occupied_and_uncontrolled_territories_of_Ukraine_(2014-present)" title="Temporarily occupied and uncontrolled territories of Ukraine (2014-present)">Donetsk, Luhansk and Crimea</a> regions affected by Russian military intervention of 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NMC20416_271-0"><a href="#cite_note-NMC20416-271">[269]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_response">Russian response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Russian response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/2014_anti-war_protests_in_Russia" title="2014 anti-war protests in Russia">2014 anti-war protests in Russia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2014-03-10_-_Yevpatoria_military_base_-_0017.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3629" data-file-width="2645" height="302" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/2014-03-10_-_Yevpatoria_military_base_-_0017.JPG/220px-2014-03-10_-_Yevpatoria_military_base_-_0017.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/2014-03-10_-_Yevpatoria_military_base_-_0017.JPG/330px-2014-03-10_-_Yevpatoria_military_base_-_0017.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/2014-03-10_-_Yevpatoria_military_base_-_0017.JPG/440px-2014-03-10_-_Yevpatoria_military_base_-_0017.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2014-03-10_-_Yevpatoria_military_base_-_0017.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Request ("ultimatum") by <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Crimea" title="Council of Ministers of Crimea">Council of Ministers of Crimea</a> to Ukrainian 55th Anti-Aircraft Artillery regiment in <a href="/wiki/Yevpatoria" title="Yevpatoria">Yevpatoria</a> to lay down arms under control of <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Black Sea Fleet">Russian Black Sea Fleet</a> for the period of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimean_referendum,_2014" title="Crimean referendum, 2014">Crimean referendum</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In a poll published on 24 February by the state-owned <a href="/wiki/Russian_Public_Opinion_Research_Center" title="Russian Public Opinion Research Center">Russian Public Opinion Research Center</a>, only 15% of those Russians polled said 'yes' to the question: "Should Russia react to the overthrow of the legally elected authorities in Ukraine?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[270]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/State_Duma" title="State Duma">State Duma</a> Committee on <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> Affairs, headed by <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Slutsky_(politician)" title="Leonid Slutsky (politician)">Leonid Slutsky</a>, visited Simferopol on 25 February 2014 and said: "If the parliament of the Crimean autonomy or its residents express the wish to join the Russian Federation, Russia will be prepared to consider this sort of application. We will be examining the situation and doing so fast."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothkopf_273-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rothkopf-273">[271]</a></sup> They also stated that in the event of a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a> for Crimea region joining Russian Federation they would consider its results "very fast".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gordonua.com_274-0"><a href="#cite_note-gordonua.com-274">[272]</a></sup> Later Slutsky announced that he was misunderstood by Crimean press and no decision regarding simplifying the process of acquiring Russian citizenship for people in Crimea has been made yet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aif.ru_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-aif.ru-275">[273]</a></sup> And added that if "fellow Russian citizens are in jeopardy you understand that we do not stay away".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[274]</a></sup> On 25 February, in a meeting with Crimean politicians he stated that Viktor Yanukovych was still the legitimate president of Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[275]</a></sup> That same day in the Russian Duma, they announced they were determining measures so that Russians in Ukraine who "did not want to break from the Russian World" could acquire Russian citizenship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.D0.98.D0.BD.D1.82.D0.B5.D1.80.D1.84.D0.B0.D0.BA.D1.81_Interfax_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-.D0.98.D0.BD.D1.82.D0.B5.D1.80.D1.84.D0.B0.D0.BA.D1.81_Interfax-278">[276]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 26 February, Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> ordered the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Armed_Forces" title="Russian Armed Forces">Russian Armed Forces</a> to be "put on alert in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Military_District" title="Western Military District">Western Military District</a> as well as units stationed with the 2nd Army <a href="/wiki/Central_Military_District" title="Central Military District">Central Military District</a> Command involved in aerospace defence, airborne troops and long-range military transport." Despite media speculation it was for in reaction to the events in Ukraine Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defense_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Defense (Russia)">Defence Minister</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sergei_Shoigu" title="Sergei Shoigu">Sergei Shoigu</a> said it was in separate consideration from the unrest in Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alpert_279-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alpert-279">[277]</a></sup> On 27 February 2014, the Russian government dismissed accusations about violation by the Russian side of the basic agreements in regards of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Black Sea Fleet">Black Sea Fleet</a>: "All movements of armored vehicles are undertaken in full compliance with the basic agreements and did not require any approvals".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mid.ru_280-0"><a href="#cite_note-mid.ru-280">[278]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIA_News_281-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIA_News-281">[279]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[280]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 27 February, the Russian governing agencies presented the new law project on granting citizenship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ria.ru_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-ria.ru-283">[281]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Russian Ministry of Foreign Affairs called on the West and particularly <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> to "abandon the provocative statements and respect the neutral status of Ukraine".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mid_accusations_284-0"><a href="#cite_note-mid_accusations-284">[282]</a></sup> In its statement the ministry claims that agreement on settlement of the crisis which was signed on 21 February and was witnessed by foreign ministries from Germany, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> and France has to this date, not been implemented<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mid_accusations_284-1"><a href="#cite_note-mid_accusations-284">[282]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lukin" title="Vladimir Lukin">Vladimir Lukin</a> from Russia had not signed it<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CTV_News_285-0"><a href="#cite_note-CTV_News-285">[283]</a></sup>).</p>
<p>On 28 February, according to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ITAR-TASS" title="ITAR-TASS">ITAR-TASS</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Ministry_of_Transport" title="Russian Ministry of Transport">Russian Ministry of Transport</a> discontinued its further talks with Ukraine in regards to the <a href="/wiki/Kerch_Strait_Bridge" title="Kerch Strait Bridge">Kerch Strait Bridge</a> project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[284]</a></sup> However, on 3 March <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Russia" title="Prime Minister of Russia">Prime Minister of Russia</a>, signed a <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Government_of_Russia" title="Order of the Government of Russia">decree</a> creating a subsidiary of Russian Highways (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avtodor" title="Avtodor">Avtodor</a>) to build a bridge at an unspecified location along the Kerch strait.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TV_Rain_287-0"><a href="#cite_note-TV_Rain-287">[285]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[286]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88_%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%B8_%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83_(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6000" data-file-width="4000" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88_%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%B8_%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83_%282%29.jpg/170px-%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88_%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%B8_%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88_%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%B8_%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83_%282%29.jpg/255px-%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88_%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%B8_%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88_%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%B8_%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83_%282%29.jpg/340px-%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88_%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%B8_%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88_%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80_%D0%B8_%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%B4%D1%83_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
At least 30,000 people at 15 March protests, named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014_Russian_anti-war_protests" title="2014 Russian anti-war protests">March of Peace</a>, which took place in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> a day before the Crimean referendum.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On Russian social networks there is a movement to gather volunteers who served in the Russian army to go to Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[287]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 28 February President Putin stated it was of "extreme importance of not allowing a further escalation of violence and the necessity of a rapid normalisation of the situation in Ukraine" in telephone calls with key EU leaders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CrimeaRussiaOccupation_290-0"><a href="#cite_note-CrimeaRussiaOccupation-290">[288]</a></sup> Already on 19 February the Russian Ministry of Foreign Affairs referred to the Euromaidan revolution as the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brown_revolution" title="Brown revolution">Brown revolution</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[289]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[290]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Federation_Council_(Russia)" title="Federation Council (Russia)">Federation Council</a> approved that Russia may introduce a limited contingent of Russian troops in Crimea<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (March 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> for the security of the Black Sea Fleet and the Russians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Federation_2014_293-0"><a href="#cite_note-Federation_2014-293">[291]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Moscow, on 2 March, an estimated 27,000 rallied in support of the Russian government's decision to intervene in Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csmmoscow_294-0"><a href="#cite_note-csmmoscow-294">[292]</a></sup> The rallies received considerable attention on Russian state TV and were officially sanctioned by the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csmmoscow_294-1"><a href="#cite_note-csmmoscow-294">[292]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, on 1 March, five people who were picketing next to the Federation Council building against the invasion of Ukraine were arrested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[293]</a></sup> The next day about 200 people protested at the building of the Russian Ministry of Defence in Moscow against Russian military involvement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Utro_296-0"><a href="#cite_note-Utro-296">[294]</a></sup> About 500 people also gathered to protest on the <a href="/wiki/Manezhnaya_Square,_Moscow" title="Manezhnaya Square, Moscow">Manezhnaya Square</a> in Moscow and the same number of people on the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Isaac%27s_Square" title="Saint Isaac's Square">Saint Isaac's Square</a> in Saint Petersburg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-investigator.org.ua_297-0"><a href="#cite_note-investigator.org.ua-297">[295]</a></sup> On 2 March, about eleven protesters demonstrated in <a href="/wiki/Yekaterinburg" title="Yekaterinburg">Yekaterinburg</a> against Russian involvement, with some wrapped in the Ukrainian flag.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kp.ru_298-0"><a href="#cite_note-kp.ru-298">[296]</a></sup> Protests were also held in <a href="/wiki/Chelyabinsk" title="Chelyabinsk">Chelyabinsk</a> on the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ura.ru_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-ura.ru-299">[297]</a></sup> The opposition to the military intervention was also expressed by rock musician <a href="/wiki/Andrey_Makarevich" title="Andrey Makarevich">Andrey Makarevich</a>, who wrote in particular: "You want war with Ukraine? It will not be the way <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russo-Georgian_war" title="Russo-Georgian war">it was with Abkhazia</a>: the folks on the Maidan have been hardened and know what they are fighting for – for their country, their independence. […] We have to live with them. Still neighborly. And preferably in friendship. But it's up to them how they want to live".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-novayagazeta.ru_300-0"><a href="#cite_note-novayagazeta.ru-300">[298]</a></sup> The Professor of the Department of Philosophy at the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_State_Institute_of_International_Relations" title="Moscow State Institute of International Relations">Moscow State Institute of International Relations</a> <a href="/wiki/Andrey_Zubov" title="Andrey Zubov">Andrey Zubov</a> was fired for his article in <i><a href="/wiki/Vedomosti" title="Vedomosti">Vedomosti</a></i>, criticising Russian military intervention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bershidsky_301-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bershidsky-301">[299]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 2 March, one Moscow resident protested against Russian intervention by holding "Stop the war" banner, but he was immediately harassed by passers-by and when the police was arresting him, a woman offered them fabricating a serious charge (beating up a child) against him; however, the proposal was rejected by the police.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opposed_302-0"><a href="#cite_note-opposed-302">[300]</a></sup> Andrei Zubov, a professor at the Moscow State Institute of International Relations, who compared Russian actions in Crimea to the <a href="/wiki/Anschluss" title="Anschluss">Anschluss</a> of Austria, was threatened. Akexander Chuyev, the leader of the pro-Kremlin Spravedlivaya Rossiya party, also objected to Russian intervention in Ukraine. <a href="/wiki/Boris_Akunin" title="Boris Akunin">Boris Akunin</a>, popular Russian writer, predicted that Russia's moves would lead to political and economic isolation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opposed_302-1"><a href="#cite_note-opposed-302">[300]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_answered_journalists%E2%80%99_questions_on_the_situation_in_Ukraine_(2014-03-04).jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="387" data-file-width="650" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Vladimir_Putin_answered_journalists%E2%80%99_questions_on_the_situation_in_Ukraine_%282014-03-04%29.jpeg/290px-Vladimir_Putin_answered_journalists%E2%80%99_questions_on_the_situation_in_Ukraine_%282014-03-04%29.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Vladimir_Putin_answered_journalists%E2%80%99_questions_on_the_situation_in_Ukraine_%282014-03-04%29.jpeg/435px-Vladimir_Putin_answered_journalists%E2%80%99_questions_on_the_situation_in_Ukraine_%282014-03-04%29.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Vladimir_Putin_answered_journalists%E2%80%99_questions_on_the_situation_in_Ukraine_%282014-03-04%29.jpeg/580px-Vladimir_Putin_answered_journalists%E2%80%99_questions_on_the_situation_in_Ukraine_%282014-03-04%29.jpeg 2x" width="290"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_answered_journalists%E2%80%99_questions_on_the_situation_in_Ukraine_(2014-03-04).jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> (seated, middle) speaks to the press on 4 March 2014, denouncing <a href="/wiki/2014_Ukrainian_revolution" title="2014 Ukrainian revolution">the events in Kiev</a> as an "unconstitutional coup", and insisting that Moscow has a right to protect Russians in Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[301]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>President Putin's approval rating among the Russian public has increased by nearly 10% since the crisis began, up to 71.6%, the highest in three years, according to a poll conducted by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VTSIOM" title="VTSIOM">All-Russian Center for Public Opinion Research</a>, released on 19 March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-approval_304-0"><a href="#cite_note-approval-304">[302]</a></sup> Additionally, the same poll showed that more than 90% of Russians supported unification with the Crimean Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-approval_304-1"><a href="#cite_note-approval-304">[302]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 March, at press conference in <a href="/wiki/Novo-Ogaryovo" title="Novo-Ogaryovo">Novo-Ogaryovo</a> President Putin expressed his view on the situation that if a revolution took place in Ukraine, it is a new country with which Russia did not conclude any treaties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-putin_renounced_305-0"><a href="#cite_note-putin_renounced-305">[303]</a></sup> He brought up an analogy with events of 1917 in Russia, when as a result of the revolution the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> fell apart and a new state was created.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-putin_renounced_305-1"><a href="#cite_note-putin_renounced-305">[303]</a></sup> However, he stated Ukraine would still have to honour its debts.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_(2493-24).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="434" data-file-width="650" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_%282493-24%29.jpg/290px-Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_%282493-24%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_%282493-24%29.jpg/435px-Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_%282493-24%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_%282493-24%29.jpg/580px-Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_%282493-24%29.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_(2493-24).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Around 100,000 people gathered in Crimean Sevastopol at Victory Day parade</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Russian politicians have speculated that there are already 143,000 Ukrainian refugees in Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refugees_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-refugees-306">[304]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Ukraine)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Ukraine)">Ukrainian Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a> refuted those claims of refugees increase in Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[305]</a></sup> At a briefing on 4 March 2014, the director of department of information policy of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Ukraine)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Ukraine)">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Yevhen_Perebiynis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Yevhen Perebiynis (page does not exist)">Yevhen Perebiynis</a> said that Russia was misinforming its own citizens as well as the entire international community to justify its own actions in the Crimea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[306]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 5 March, an anchor of the Russian-owned international news channel <a href="/wiki/RT_America" title="RT America">RT America</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abby_Martin_(journalist)" title="Abby Martin (journalist)">Abby Martin</a>, in an interview with <a href="/wiki/Piers_Morgan" title="Piers Morgan">Piers Morgan</a>, said she "did not agree" with how her employer RT was covering the Ukrainian crisis, but claims RT still supports her despite her differences of opinion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Piers_309-0"><a href="#cite_note-Piers-309">[307]</a></sup> Also on 5 March 2014, another RT America anchor, <a href="/wiki/Liz_Wahl" title="Liz Wahl">Liz Wahl</a>, of the network's Washington, DC bureau, resigned on air, explaining that she could not be "part of a network that whitewashes the actions of Putin" and citing her Hungarian ancestry and the memory of the Soviet repression of the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1956" title="Hungarian Revolution of 1956">Hungarian Uprising</a> as a factor in her decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kirchick_310-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kirchick-310">[308]</a></sup></p>
<p>In early March, Igor Andreyev, a 75-year-old survivor of the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Leningrad" title="Siege of Leningrad">Siege of Leningrad</a>, attended an anti-war rally against the Russian intervention in Crimea and was holding a sign that read "Peace to the World". The riot police arrested him and a local pro-government lawyer then accused him of being a supporter of "fascism". The retiree, who lived on a 6,500-ruble monthly pension, was fined 10,000 rubles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[309]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prominent dissident <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Khodorkovsky" title="Mikhail Khodorkovsky">Mikhail Khodorkovsky</a> said that Crimea should stay within Ukraine with broader autonomy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Interfax_312-0"><a href="#cite_note-Interfax-312">[310]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tatarstan" title="Tatarstan">Tatarstan</a>, a republic within Russia populated by <a href="/wiki/Volga_Tatars" title="Volga Tatars">Volga Tatars</a>, has sought to alleviate concerns about treatment of Tatars by Russia, as Tatarstan is a gas-rich and economically successful republic in Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera.com_313-0"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera.com-313">[311]</a></sup> On 5 March, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_of_Tatarstan" title="President of Tatarstan">President of Tatarstan</a> <a href="/wiki/Rustam_Minnikhanov" title="Rustam Minnikhanov">Rustam Minnikhanov</a> signed an agreement on co-operation between Tatarstan and the Aksyonov government in Crimea that implied collaboration between ten government institutions as well as significant financial aid to Crimea from Tatarstan businesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera.com_313-1"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera.com-313">[311]</a></sup> On 11 March, Minnikhanov was in Crimea on his second visit and attended as a guest present in the Crimean parliament chamber during the vote on the declaration of sovereignty pending 16 March referendum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera.com_313-2"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera.com-313">[311]</a></sup> The Tatarstan's Mufti <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kamil_Samigullin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kamil Samigullin (page does not exist)">Kamil Samigullin</a> invited Crimean Tatars to study in madrasas in Kazan and declared support for their "brothers in faith and blood".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera.com_313-3"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera.com-313">[311]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Dzhemilev" title="Mustafa Dzhemilev">Mustafa Dzhemilev</a>, a former leader of the Crimean Tatar Majlis believes that forces that are suspected to be Russian forces should leave the Crimean peninsula,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera.com_313-4"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera.com-313">[311]</a></sup> and has asked the UN Security Council to send peacekeepers into the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314">[312]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 13 March, Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> made a comparison between Crimea and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> in a phone call with US President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315">[313]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 15 March, thousands of protesters (estimates varying from 3,000 by official sources up to 50,000 claimed by opposition) in Moscow marched against Russian involvement in Ukraine, many waving Ukrainian flags.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[314]</a></sup> At the same time a pro government (and pro-<a href="/wiki/Crimean_status_referendum,_2014" title="Crimean status referendum, 2014">referendum</a>) rally, occurred across the street, counted thousands as well (officials claiming 27,000 with opposition claiming about 10,000).</p>
<p>In February 2015, the leading independent Russian newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Novaya_Gazeta" title="Novaya Gazeta">Novaya Gazeta</a></i> reported<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Novaya_predstavlyaetsya_317-0"><a href="#cite_note-Novaya_predstavlyaetsya-317">[315]</a></sup> that it obtained documents, allegedly written by oligarch Konstantin Malofayev and others, which provided the Russian government with a strategy in the event of Viktor Yanukovych's removal from power and the break-up of Ukraine, which were considered likely. The documents outline plans for annexation of Crimea and the eastern portions of the country, closely describing the events that actually followed after Yanukovych's fall. The documents also describe plans for a public relations campaign which would seek to justify Russian actions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[316]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[317]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[318]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2015 <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Kasyanov" title="Mikhail Kasyanov">Mikhail Kasyanov</a> stated that all Russian Duma decisions on Crimea annexation were illegal from the international point of view and the annexation was provoked by false accusations of discrimination of Russian nationals in Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[319]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_response">International response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: International response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Crimea" title="Political status of Crimea">Political status of Crimea</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_68/262" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 68/262">United Nations General Assembly Resolution 68/262</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_reactions_to_the_2014_Crimean_crisis" title="International reactions to the 2014 Crimean crisis">International reactions to the 2014 Crimean crisis</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crimea_reaction_clean.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="387" data-file-width="825" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Crimea_reaction_clean.svg/300px-Crimea_reaction_clean.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Crimea_reaction_clean.svg/450px-Crimea_reaction_clean.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Crimea_reaction_clean.svg/600px-Crimea_reaction_clean.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

International reaction to the 2014 Crimean crisis according to official governmental statements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322"><a href="#cite_note-322">[b]</a></sup>

<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #6a1f1f; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <i>Russia</i></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #CDCDCD; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <i>No official statements / No data available</i></div>
