</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UN_Resolution_regarding_the_territorial_integrity_of_Ukraine.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="940" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/UN_Resolution_regarding_the_territorial_integrity_of_Ukraine.svg/300px-UN_Resolution_regarding_the_territorial_integrity_of_Ukraine.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/UN_Resolution_regarding_the_territorial_integrity_of_Ukraine.svg/450px-UN_Resolution_regarding_the_territorial_integrity_of_Ukraine.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/UN_Resolution_regarding_the_territorial_integrity_of_Ukraine.svg/600px-UN_Resolution_regarding_the_territorial_integrity_of_Ukraine.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UN_Resolution_regarding_the_territorial_integrity_of_Ukraine.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Results of the United Nations General Assembly vote about the territorial integrity of Ukraine.<br/>
<span style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #74C365; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> In favour <span style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ab4e52; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Against <span style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FADA5E; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Abstentions <span class="nowrap"><span style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #89CFF0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Absent</span> <span style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #e0e0e0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Non-members</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There have been a range of international reactions to the annexation. The UN General Assembly passed a non-binding resolution 100 in favour, 11 against and 58 abstentions in the 193-nation assembly that declared invalid Crimea's Moscow-backed referendum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CHARBONNEAU_AND_DONATH_323-0"><a href="#cite_note-CHARBONNEAU_AND_DONATH-323">[320]</a></sup> In a move supported by the Lithuanian President,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNBC_324-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNBC-324">[321]</a></sup> the United States government imposed sanctions against persons they deem to have violated or assisted in the violation of Ukraine's sovereignty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EO13660_325-0"><a href="#cite_note-EO13660-325">[322]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> suspended talks with Russia on economic and visa-related matters, and is considering more stringent sanctions against Russia in the near future, including asset freezes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUsanctions_326-0"><a href="#cite_note-EUsanctions-326">[323]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mainichi.jp_327-0"><a href="#cite_note-mainichi.jp-327">[324]</a></sup> while Japan announced sanctions which include suspension of talks relating to military, space, investment, and visa requirements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328">[325]</a></sup> The United Kingdom qualified the referendum vote in Crimea of being "farcical", "illegal" and "illegitimate".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329"><a href="#cite_note-329">[326]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU_Commission" title="EU Commission">EU Commission</a> decided on 11 March to enter into a full free-trade agreement with Ukraine within the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-330"><a href="#cite_note-330">[327]</a></sup> On 12 March, the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> rejected the upcoming referendum on independence in Crimea, which they saw as manipulated and contrary to international and Ukrainian law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-331"><a href="#cite_note-331">[328]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G7" title="G7">G7</a> bloc of developed nations (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G8" title="G8">G8</a> minus Russia) made a joint statement condemning Russia and announced that they would suspend preparations for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/40th_G8_summit" title="40th G8 summit">the planned G8 summit</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sochi" title="Sochi">Sochi</a> in June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-332"><a href="#cite_note-332">[329]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-333"><a href="#cite_note-333">[330]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> condemned Russia's military escalation in Crimea and stated that it was breach of international law<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-334"><a href="#cite_note-334">[331]</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> expressed its full support for the territorial integrity and national unity of Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-335"><a href="#cite_note-335">[332]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="Visegrád Group">Visegrád Group</a> has issued a joint statement urging Russia to respect Ukraine's territorial integrity and for Ukraine to take into account its minority groups to not further break fragile relations. It has urged for Russia to respect Ukrainian and international law and in line with the provisions of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1994_Budapest_Memorandum" title="1994 Budapest Memorandum">1994 Budapest Memorandum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Visegrad_336-0"><a href="#cite_note-Visegrad-336">[333]</a></sup></p>
<p>China said "We respect the independence, sovereignty and territorial integrity of Ukraine". A spokesman restated China's belief of non-interference in the internal affairs of other nations and urged dialogue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtbacchi1_337-0"><a href="#cite_note-ibtbacchi1-337">[334]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtbacchi2_338-0"><a href="#cite_note-ibtbacchi2-338">[335]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/National_Security_Advisor_(India)" title="National Security Advisor (India)">National Security Advisor</a> <a href="/wiki/Shivshankar_Menon" title="Shivshankar Menon">Shivshankar Menon</a> of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> stated that Russia has legitimate interests in Crimea and called for "sustained diplomatic efforts" and "constructive dialogue" to resolve the crisis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-339"><a href="#cite_note-339">[336]</a></sup> However, the National Security Advisor is not a part of the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">Cabinet</a> of India and, as such, Menon's statement was not an official statement issued by the government of India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340"><a href="#cite_note-340">[337]</a></sup> However, India subsequently made it clear that it will not support any "unilateral measures" against Russian government. "India has never supported unilateral sanctions against any country. Therefore, we will also not support any unilateral measures by a country or a group of countries against Russia."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-341"><a href="#cite_note-341">[338]</a></sup> Both <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> openly support Russian military action. Syrian President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bashar_al_Assad" title="Bashar al Assad">Bashar al Assad</a> said that he supports Putin's efforts to "restore security and stability in the friendly country of Ukraine", while Venezuelan President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nicolas_Maduro" title="Nicolas Maduro">Nicolas Maduro</a> condemned Ukraine's "ultra-nationalist" coup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-342"><a href="#cite_note-342">[339]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFGATE_343-0"><a href="#cite_note-SFGATE-343">[340]</a></sup> Sri Lanka described Yanukovych's removal as unconstitutional and considered Russia's concerns in Crimea as justified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-344"><a href="#cite_note-344">[341]</a></sup></p>
<p>Polish Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Donald_Tusk" title="Donald Tusk">Donald Tusk</a> called for change in EU energy policy as Germany's dependence on Russian gas poses risks for Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuardianRussiaMerkel_345-0"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianRussiaMerkel-345">[342]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 13 March, German Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> warned the Russian government it risks massive damage to Russia, economically and politically, if it refuses to change course on Ukraine,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuardianRussiaMerkel_345-1"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianRussiaMerkel-345">[342]</a></sup> though close economic links between Germany and Russia significantly reduce the scope for any sanctions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-346"><a href="#cite_note-346">[343]</a></sup></p>
<p>After Russia moved to formally incorporate Crimea, some worried whether it may do the same in other regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Transdniester_347-0"><a href="#cite_note-Transdniester-347">[344]</a></sup> US deputy national security advisor <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blinken" title="Tony Blinken">Tony Blinken</a> said that the Russian troops massed on the eastern Ukrainian border may be preparing to enter the country's eastern regions. Russian officials stated that Russian troops would not enter other areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Transdniester_347-1"><a href="#cite_note-Transdniester-347">[344]</a></sup> US Air Force Gen. <a href="/wiki/Philip_M._Breedlove" title="Philip M. Breedlove">Philip M. Breedlove</a>, NATO's supreme allied commander in Europe, warned that the same troops were in a position to take over the separatist Russian-speaking <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldovan</a> province of <a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Transdniester_347-2"><a href="#cite_note-Transdniester-347">[344]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 9 April, the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Assembly_of_the_Council_of_Europe" title="Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe">Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe</a> deprived Russia of voting rights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-348"><a href="#cite_note-348">[345]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 August, while visiting Crimea, Vladimir Putin ruled out pushing beyond Crimea. He undertook to do everything he could to end the conflict in Ukraine, saying Russia needed to build calmly and with dignity, not by confrontation and war which isolated it from the rest of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PutinConciliatory_349-0"><a href="#cite_note-PutinConciliatory-349">[346]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Nations_resolutions">United Nations resolutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: United Nations resolutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">

<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #89CFF0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Absent when the vote took place</div>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Security_Council_resolution">Security Council resolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Security Council resolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_vetoed_United_Nations_Security_Council_resolutions" title="List of vetoed United Nations Security Council resolutions">List of vetoed United Nations Security Council resolutions</a></div>
<p>On 15 March 2014, a US-sponsored resolution that went to a vote in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a> to reaffirm that council's commitment to Ukraine's "sovereignty, independence, unity and territorial integrity" was not approved. Though a total of 13 council members voted in favour of the resolution and China abstained, Russia vetoed the resolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-350"><a href="#cite_note-350">[347]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="General_Assembly_resolution">General Assembly resolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: General Assembly resolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 27 March 2014, the UN General Assembly approved a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_68/262" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 68/262">resolution</a> describing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimean_referendum,_2014" title="Crimean referendum, 2014">referendum</a> leading to annexation of Crimea by Russia as illegal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-351"><a href="#cite_note-351">[348]</a></sup> The draft resolution, which was titled "Territorial integrity of Ukraine", was co-sponsored by Canada, Costa Rica, Germany, Lithuania, Poland, Ukraine and the US. It affirmed the council's commitment to the "sovereignty, political independence, unity and territorial integrity of Ukraine within its internationally recognised borders." The resolution tried to underscore that 16 March referendum held in Crimea and the city of Sevastopol has no validity and cannot form the basis for any alteration of the status of the Autonomous Republic of Crimea or of the city of Sevastopol. The resolution got 100 votes in its favour, while 11 nations voted against and 58 countries abstained from the vote. The resolution was non-binding and the vote was largely symbolic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-352"><a href="#cite_note-352">[349]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition">Recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The vast majority of the international community has not recognised the Republic of Crimea and Sevastopol as part of Russia. Most nations in North America, Central America, Europe, Oceania, and Africa, as well as Asia outside of the former Soviet republics, have openly rejected the referendum and the accession, and instead consider Crimea and Sevastopol to be administrative divisions of Ukraine. The remainder have largely remained neutral. The vote on <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_68/262" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 68/262">United Nations General Assembly Resolution 68/262</a> (supporting the position that Crimea and Sevastopol remain part of Ukraine) was 100 to 11 in favour, with 58 states abstaining and a further 24 of the 193 member states not voting through being absent when the vote took place.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a> have recognised the Republic of Crimea and the City of Sevastopol as federal subjects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-353"><a href="#cite_note-353">[350]</a></sup></p>
<p>The position of <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> is vague: it includes statements made by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Lukashenko" title="Alexander Lukashenko">Alexander Lukashenko</a> that "Ukraine should remain an integral, indivisible, non-aligned state" and "As for Crimea, I do not like it when the integrity and independence of a country are broken", on the one hand, and "Today Crimea is part of the Russian Federation. No matter whether you recognize it or not, the fact remains." and "Whether Crimea will be recognised as a region of the Russian Federation de-jure does not really matter", on the other hand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-354"><a href="#cite_note-354">[351]</a></sup></p>
<p>Three <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">non-UN member states</a> recognised the results of the referendum: <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia">South Ossetia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_Republic" title="Nagorno-Karabakh Republic">Nagorno-Karabakh</a>. A fourth, <a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistria</a>, sent a request on 18 March 2014 to join the Russian Federation following the Crimean example and in compliance with the Admission Law provisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-355"><a href="#cite_note-355">[352]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-356"><a href="#cite_note-356">[353]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-357"><a href="#cite_note-357">[354]</a></sup> On 16 April 2014 Transnistria urged Russia and the United Nations to recognise its independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-358"><a href="#cite_note-358">[355]</a></sup> Putin is aware of Transnistria's recognition request, according to <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Peskov" title="Dmitry Peskov">Dmitry Peskov</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-359"><a href="#cite_note-359">[356]</a></sup> The regional council of Italy's northern region <a href="/wiki/Lombardy" title="Lombardy">Lombardy</a> has adopted a non-binding resolution on recognizing Crimea as part of Russia. The document also calls on the central government to work out a plan to lift the sanctions from Moscow, local news agency Il Giorno reports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-360"><a href="#cite_note-360">[357]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sanctions">Sanctions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sanctions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/International_sanctions_during_the_Ukrainian_crisis" title="International sanctions during the Ukrainian crisis">International sanctions during the Ukrainian crisis</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_individuals_sanctioned_during_the_Ukrainian_crisis" title="List of individuals sanctioned during the Ukrainian crisis">List of individuals sanctioned during the Ukrainian crisis</a></div>
<p>Sanctions were imposed to prevent Russian and Crimean officials and politicians travelling to Canada, the United States, and the European Union. They were the most wide-ranging used on Russia since the fall of the Soviet Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Katakey_361-0"><a href="#cite_note-Katakey-361">[358]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-362"><a href="#cite_note-362">[359]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-363"><a href="#cite_note-363">[360]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-364"><a href="#cite_note-364">[361]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sanctions_365-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sanctions-365">[362]</a></sup></p>
<p>Japan announced milder sanctions than the US and EU. These include suspension of talks relating to military, space, investment, and visa requirements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-366"><a href="#cite_note-366">[363]</a></sup></p>
<p>In response to the sanctions introduced by the US and EU, the <a href="/wiki/State_Duma" title="State Duma">Russian Duma</a> unanimously passed a resolution asking for all members of the Duma to be included on the sanctions list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dumasanctions_367-0"><a href="#cite_note-dumasanctions-367">[364]</a></sup> Head of the opposition <a href="/wiki/A_Just_Russia" title="A Just Russia">A Just Russia</a> party <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sergei_Mironov" title="Sergei Mironov">Sergei Mironov</a> said he was proud of being included on the sanctions list, "It is with pride that I have found myself on the black list, this means they have noticed my stance on Crimea."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dumasanctions_367-1"><a href="#cite_note-dumasanctions-367">[364]</a></sup> Russian companies started pulling billions of dollars out of Western banks to avoid any asset freeze.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FT_freeze_368-0"><a href="#cite_note-FT_freeze-368">[365]</a></sup></p>
<p>Three days after the lists were published, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_Ministry_of_Russia" title="Foreign Ministry of Russia">Russian Foreign Ministry</a> published a reciprocal sanctions list of US citizens, which consisted of 10 names, including House of Representatives Speaker <a href="/wiki/John_Boehner" title="John Boehner">John Boehner</a>, Senator <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a>, and two advisers to President Obama. The ministry said in the statement, "Treating our country in such way, as Washington could have already ascertained, is inappropriate and counterproductive," and reiterated that sanctions against Russia would have a boomerang effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-369"><a href="#cite_note-369">[366]</a></sup> Several of those sanctioned responded with pride at their inclusion on the list, including <a href="/wiki/John_Boehner" title="John Boehner">John Boehner</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WaPo_370-0"><a href="#cite_note-WaPo-370">[367]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WaPo_370-1"><a href="#cite_note-WaPo-370">[367]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bob_Menendez" title="Bob Menendez">Bob Menendez</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-371"><a href="#cite_note-371">[368]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dan_Coats" title="Dan Coats">Dan Coats</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WaPo_370-2"><a href="#cite_note-WaPo-370">[367]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mary_Landrieu" title="Mary Landrieu">Mary Landrieu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Harry_Reid" title="Harry Reid">Harry Reid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-372"><a href="#cite_note-372">[369]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 March, Russia has imposed retaliatory sanctions on 13 Canadian officials including members of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Canada" title="Parliament of Canada">Parliament of Canada</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chaseglobeandmail_373-0"><a href="#cite_note-chaseglobeandmail-373">[370]</a></sup> banning them from entering Russia. Foreign Affairs Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Baird_(Canadian_politician)" title="John Baird (Canadian politician)">John Baird</a>, said the sanctions were "a badge of honour."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-374"><a href="#cite_note-374">[371]</a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Justice_(Canada)" title="Minister of Justice (Canada)">Minister of Justice</a> <a href="/wiki/Irwin_Cotler" title="Irwin Cotler">Irwin Cotler</a> also said that he considered the sanctions a badge of honour, not a mark of exclusion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chaseglobeandmail_373-1"><a href="#cite_note-chaseglobeandmail-373">[370]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2014, <i>The Christian Science Monitor</i> reported, "The good news is that so far, Russia has shown no inclination to use the NDN [ <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Distribution_Network" title="Northern Distribution Network">Northern Distribution Network</a>, key supply line to <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> that runs through Russia] as leverage in the wake of US retaliation for its troop movements in Crimea."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-375"><a href="#cite_note-375">[372]</a></sup></p>
<p>Expanded Western sanctions in mid-March coursed through financial markets, hitting the business interests of some Russia's richest people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FT_share_prices_376-0"><a href="#cite_note-FT_share_prices-376">[373]</a></sup> The Americans centred on the heart of Moscow's leadership,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-377"><a href="#cite_note-377">[374]</a></sup> though the EU's initial list shied from targeting Putin's inner circle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-378"><a href="#cite_note-378">[375]</a></sup> As ratings agencies <a href="/wiki/Fitch_Ratings" title="Fitch Ratings">Fitch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor's">Standard &amp; Poor's</a> downgraded Russia's credit outlook,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_downgrade_379-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_downgrade-379">[376]</a></sup> Russian banks warned of a sanctions-induced recession,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-380"><a href="#cite_note-380">[377]</a></sup> the country braced for capital outflows for the first three months of 2014 to reach $70 billion,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-381"><a href="#cite_note-381">[378]</a></sup> more than the entirety of outflows for 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-382"><a href="#cite_note-382">[379]</a></sup> and Russian government-bond issues plummeted by three-quarters compared with the same period the previous year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-383"><a href="#cite_note-383">[380]</a></sup> Novatek, Russia's second-largest gas producer, saw $2.5bn in market value wiped out when its shares sank by nearly 10%, rendering Putin's close friend <a href="/wiki/Gennady_Timchenko" title="Gennady Timchenko">Gennady Timchenko</a>, who has a 23% stake in the company, $575m poorer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FT_share_prices_376-1"><a href="#cite_note-FT_share_prices-376">[373]</a></sup> "I do hope that there is some serious diplomatic activity going on behind the scenes," said one Russian banker,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-384"><a href="#cite_note-384">[381]</a></sup> though others were more sanguine on the question of whether the sanctions would have any enduring effect,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_downgrade_379-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_downgrade-379">[376]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-385"><a href="#cite_note-385">[382]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-386"><a href="#cite_note-386">[383]</a></sup> and Russians, top and bottom, seemed defiant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-387"><a href="#cite_note-387">[384]</a></sup> The official Russian response was mixed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-388"><a href="#cite_note-388">[385]</a></sup></p>
<p>Minister of Economic Development of the Russian Federation <a href="/wiki/Alexey_Ulyukaev" title="Alexey Ulyukaev">Alexey Ulyukaev</a> said what introduction of sectoral sanctions will lead to a serious decline of the Russian economy: economic growth of Russia will become seriously negative, the growth of volumes of investment will be even more negative, inflation will be on the rise, and government revenues and reserves will go down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-389"><a href="#cite_note-389">[386]</a></sup></p>
<p>As well as differences between the United States and Europe as a whole as to how to respond to the Russian-backed incursion, those same differences have played out among Eastern European countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-390"><a href="#cite_note-390">[387]</a></sup></p>
<p>A number of Russian citizens reported that they have been denied European visas after they visited Crimea after annexation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-391"><a href="#cite_note-391">[388]</a></sup> A Russian consumer protection watchdog OZPP published a warning for Russian tourists about this risk, explaining that from the international law point of view Crimea is an occupied territory, after which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roskomnadzor" title="Roskomnadzor">Roskomnadzor</a> blocked the OZPP website "for threatenting territorial integrity of Russian federation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-392"><a href="#cite_note-392">[389]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mapping">Mapping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Mapping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>As of March 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> still maps Crimea as belonging to Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-393"><a href="#cite_note-393">[390]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Society" title="National Geographic Society">National Geographic Society</a> stated that their policy is "to portray current reality" and "Crimea, if it is formally annexed by Russia, would be shaded gray", but also further remarked that this step does not suggest recognising legitimacy of such.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-394"><a href="#cite_note-394">[391]</a></sup> As of April 2014 Crimea is still displayed as part of Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hitechmaps_395-0"><a href="#cite_note-hitechmaps-395">[392]</a></sup></li>
<li>As of April 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Google_Maps" title="Google Maps">Google Maps</a> displays Crimea as a disputed territory to most viewers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hitechmaps_395-1"><a href="#cite_note-hitechmaps-395">[392]</a></sup> For the Russian and Ukrainian versions of website, Crimea is marked as belonging to corresponding country (Russia or Ukraine respectively).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hitechmaps_395-2"><a href="#cite_note-hitechmaps-395">[392]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-396"><a href="#cite_note-396">[393]</a></sup> Google stated that it "work(s) with sources to get the best interpretation of the border or claim lines".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-397"><a href="#cite_note-397">[394]</a></sup></li>
<li>As of April 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Yandex" title="Yandex">Yandex</a> displays Crimea as Russian, except for users entering from their Ukrainian site and their Turkish site. Users visiting Yandex.ru from Russia will see Crimea displayed as Russian territory, users visiting yandex.ua from Ukraine will see Crimea as Ukrainian and all other users (from other countries)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Needs to be verified as Turkish Yandex depicts Crimea as being Ukraine (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> will see Crimea as Russian territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hitechmaps_395-3"><a href="#cite_note-hitechmaps-395">[392]</a></sup> According to official statement, the company works with users from different countries and "displays reality that surrounds them".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-398"><a href="#cite_note-398">[395]</a></sup></li>
<li>As of March 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Bing_Maps" title="Bing Maps">Bing Maps</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-399"><a href="#cite_note-399">[396]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/OpenStreetMap" title="OpenStreetMap">OpenStreetMap</a> and <a href="/wiki/Here_(company)" title="Here (company)">HERE</a> display Crimea as belonging to Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hitechmaps_395-4"><a href="#cite_note-hitechmaps-395">[392]</a></sup> In particular, Open Street Map requested its users to refrain from editing borders and administrative relations of subdivisions located in Autonomous Republic of Crimea and Sevastopol until 31 May 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hitechmaps_395-5"><a href="#cite_note-hitechmaps-395">[392]</a></sup> On 5 June 2014 <a href="/wiki/OpenStreetMap" title="OpenStreetMap">OpenStreetMap</a> switched to a territorial dispute option, displaying Crimea as a disputed territory belonging to both countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-400"><a href="#cite_note-400">[397]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2015, on the <a href="/wiki/PepsiCo" title="PepsiCo">PepsiCo</a> website it was visible for a few days a Russian-language map depicting Crimea as part of Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-401"><a href="#cite_note-401">[398]</a></sup></li>
<li>The 2016 edition of a French atlas published by <a href="/wiki/%C3%89ditions_Larousse" title="Éditions Larousse">Larousse</a> shows Crimea as part of Russian territory: <a href="/wiki/Oleh_Shamshur" title="Oleh Shamshur">Oleh Shamshur</a>, Ukrainian Ambassador to France, expressed shock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-402"><a href="#cite_note-402">[399]</a></sup> Shortly after, Larousse corrected the mistake on the Atlas on their internet version,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-403"><a href="#cite_note-403">[400]</a></sup> and confirmed that Crimea is a region of Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-404"><a href="#cite_note-404">[401]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_impact">Economic impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economic impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(June 2015)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>While initially (right after the annexation), salaries rose, especially those of government workers, this was soon offset by the increase in prices caused by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Russian_financial_crisis" title="2014–15 Russian financial crisis">depreciation of the ruble</a>. Subsequently, after Russian authority became established, wages were cut back again by 30% to 70%. Tourism, previously Crimea's main industry, suffered in particular; it was down by 50% from 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-405"><a href="#cite_note-405">[402]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-406"><a href="#cite_note-406">[403]</a></sup> Crimean agricultural yields were also significantly impacted by the annexation. Ukraine cut off supplies of water through the <a href="/wiki/North_Crimean_Canal" title="North Crimean Canal">North Crimean Canal</a>, causing the 2014 rice crop to fail, and greatly damaging the <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soybean" title="Soybean">soybean</a> crops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6ME_407-0"><a href="#cite_note-6ME-407">[404]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">

<li id="cite_note-143"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-143">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Dilanian (2014) "CIA director John Brennan told a senior lawmaker Monday that a 1997 treaty between Russia and Ukraine allows up to 25,000 Russia troops in the vital Crimea region, so Russia may not consider its recent troop movements to be an invasion, U.S. officials said."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dilanian_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dilanian-142">[141]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-322"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-322">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">If an official position can be sorted in more than one category, the "strongest" position was marked (from the "call for a peaceful resolution" to "interpretation as a military intervention" consecutively). For the sources see the image description.</span></li>
</ol>

<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-84">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It also noted that "certain politicians, local government officials, leaders of civil society organizations, and radically inclined individuals have attempted to create grounds for escalating the civil conflict, and have spread autonomous and separatist attitudes among the people, which could lead to the demise of our as a united nation and loss of its national sovereignty." In addition, the statement said that certain lawmakers of every level have begun separatist negotiations with representatives of foreign nations. "Open consultations are being held on the possible division of the country into separate parts in violation of the Ukrainian constitution," read the statement. "This could lead to an escalation of conflict between different sectors of society, inciting ethnic or religious hatred and military conflict."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kp21live_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-kp21live-83">[83]</a></sup></span></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">

<li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-52">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"The Crimean Tatars began repatriating on a massive scale beginning in the late 1980s and continuing into the early 1990s. The population of Crimean Tatars in Crimea rapidly reached 250,000 and leveled off at 270,000 where it remains as of this writing [2001]. There are believed to be between 30,000 and 100,000 remaining in places of former exile in Central Asia." Greta Lynn Uehling, <i>The Crimean Tatars</i> (Encyclopedia of the Minorities, Chicago: Fitzroy Dearborn) <a class="external text" href="http://www.iccrimea.org/scholarly/krimtatars.html" rel="nofollow">iccrimea.org</a></span></li>
